Rashi on Numbers
רש"י על במדבר
Rashi Chumash, Metsudah Publications, 2009
https://www.nli.org.il/he/books/NNL_ALEPH002691623

Rashi on Numbers



Chapter 1



Verse 1

<b>In the Sinai desert . . . on the first [day] of the [second] month, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because they (the Israelites) are precious before Him (Hashem), He counts them all the time; when they went out of Egypt He counted them [Shemos, 12:37], and when they fell because of [the sin of] the golden calf He counted them <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to know the number of those who remained, when He came to cause His Presence to rest upon them He counted them. On the first day of Nisan the <i>Mishkon</i> was set up, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and on the first day of Iyar He counted them. 

Verse 2

<b>According to their families.</b> To know <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the number of each tribe
<b>To the house of their fathers:</b> Someone whose father is from one tribe and his mother from another tribe shall be <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>maintained in his father’s tribe.
<b>Individually</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Through the <i>shekolim</i> a half-<i>shekel</i> per head.

Verse 3

<b>All those eligible for the army.</b> This teaches us that no one is eligible for the army <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>below the age of twenty. 


Verse 4

<b>Along with you, there shall be.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When you count them, there shall be with you the leader of each tribe. 


Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>These are the ones called from the congregation.</b> The ones who were invited <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to everything of importance in the congregation.

Verse 17

<b>These men.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Those twelve leaders [mentioned above, 5–15]. 
<b>Who were designated:</b> To him (Moshe) here by [their] names.

Verse 18

<b>And they were registered by family ancestry.</b> They brought their <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>genealogical documents and witnesses who <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>verified the status of their birth, this applied to each individual, to establish their kinship with the tribe.

Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24

Verse 26

Verse 40



Verse 41



Verse 42



Verse 43



Verse 44



Verse 45



Verse 46



Verse 47



Verse 48



Verse 49

<b>However, the tribe of Levi you shall not count.</b> The King’s legion is worthy of being <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>counted separately. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation; the Holy One, blessed is He, foresaw that a decree would arise against all those who were counted from the age of twenty and above to die in the desert. He [therefore] said, “Let these [Levites] not be included, for they are mine, since they did not sin with the [golden] calf.” 

Verse 50

<b>You shall appoint the Levites.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] translates, “appoint.” The word denotes appointment to <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>authority over the subject of one’s appointment, as, “and let the king appoint officials.” (Esther 2) 


Verse 51

<b>[They] shall take it down.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As Targum (Onkelos) translates, “they shall dismantle.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When they were going to depart in the desert from journey to journey they would dismantle it (the <i>Mishkon</i>) from its upright position and carry it to the place where the cloud came to rest. They camped there and set it up. 
<b>And the stranger who approaches:</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To [perform] this service of theirs.
<b>Shall die:</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>By the hand of heaven.

Verse 52

<b>And each man at his own banner.</b> According to the way that the banners are arranged in this book (i.e., Bamidbar, 2:3–31), three tribes to each banner. 

Verse 53

<b>So that there will not be anger.</b> If you fulfill My commandments there will not be anger, but if not — if strangers will enter into this service of theirs — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>there will be anger, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as we find in the episode of Korach, “. . . for the anger had emerged . . .” [17:11] 


Chapter 2



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>With the insignia.</b> Each banner shall have [as] its insignia a colored cloth hanging from it. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Each one’s color was not like the other’s, each color corresponded with the hue of its gem set in the breastplate. Thusly, everyone could recognize his banner. Another interpretation [of] “with the insignia of their fathers’ houses”; By the sign their forefather Yaakov gave them <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>when they carried him from Egypt [for burial in Canaan], as it is said, “And his sons did to him just as he had commanded them” [Bereishis, 50:12]. ‘Yehudah, Yissachar, and Zevulun shall carry him from the east, Reuven, Shimon, and Gad from the south; etc.,’ as stated by Tanchuma to this portion. 

<b>At a distance:</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>At the distance of a <i>mil</i> (2,000 <i>amos,</i> approximately 4,000 feet.) as stated in the Book of Joshua [3:4], ‘However, there should be a distance between you and it (the sacred ark) of two thousand <i>amos</i>’, To enable them to come on Shabbos. Moshe and Aharon and his sons and the Levites camped near it (the <i>Mishkon</i>). 

Verse 3

<b>In the forefront.</b> Toward the side called קֶדֶם, the front. Which is this? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is the eastern side whereas the west is called אָחוֹר, the rear. 


Verse 4



Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9

<b>They travel first.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When they see the cloud rise, the <i>kohanim</i> blow the trumpets and the camp of Yehudah departs first. When traveling, they move <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the way they camped; The Levites and the wagons at the center, the banner of Yehudah to the east, that of Reuven to the south, Ephraim's to the west, and Don’s to the north. 


Verse 10



Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>The Tent of Meeting shall travel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>After those two banners.
<b>Just as they camp, so shall they travel:</b> As I explained, they traveled as they camped, each banner proceeding in its designated position. 
<b>In his place [literally “his hand”]</b> In his place. Yet, the literal meaning, “his hand” is not out of context. One’s nearby area is called “at hand,” [i.e.,] adjacent, within hand’s reach. <i>en son aise,</i> at hand, in Old French. 

Verse 18



Verse 19



Verse 20

<b>With him [literally “above him”].</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As Targum [Onkelos] translates, “the one near him.” 


Chapter 3



Verse 1

<b>These are the descendants of Aharon and Moshe.</b> [Scripture] mentions only the sons of Aharon, yet they are called the descendants of Moshe — because he taught them Torah. This teaches us that one who teaches another’s son Torah is considered as having procreated him. 
<b>On the day that Adonoy spoke to Moshe</b> They became his descendants, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>since he taught them what he had learned from the mouth of the Almighty. 

Verse 2



Verse 3



Verse 4

<b>In the presence [literally “the face”] of Aharon.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>During his lifetime. 


Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>And they shall serve him.</b> What is the service? [The next passage explains —] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”They shall preserve his guardianship;” since he (Aharon) is obligated to guard the Sanctuary so that no stranger may approach, as it is said, “. . . you (Aharon), your sons, and your father’s house with you shall bear [responsibility for] the sin of [defiling] the Sanctuary . . .,” and these Levites aided them, this is the service. 

Verse 7

<b>They shall take care to preserve his guardianship.</b> Any position to which a person is appointed which requires his active management is called a “watch” throughout Scripture, and in the Mishnaic idiom, as stated concerning Bigsan and Seresh, “But surely my watch is not similar to yours”? Similarly, the “watches” of the <i>kohanim</i> and Levites. 


Verse 8

<b>And the watch of Bnei Yisroel.</b> They were all actually obligated to provide the needs of the Sanctuary; the Levites merely served in their place, as surrogates. This is why they (the Levites) accepted the tithes from them, in payment, as it is said, “. . . for it (the tithe) is your payment, in return for your service . . .” 

Verse 9

<b>They are presented to him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>For assistance.
<b>From [among] Bnei Yisroel</b> This [מֵאֵת, “from”] is understood as מִתּוֹךְ, “from among” Bnei Yisroel, meaning <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>from the rest of the entire congregation they (the Levites) were selected for this by Divine decree and He (God) gave them to him (Aharon), as it is said, “I (God) have given the Levites, given [them] . . .” 


Verse 10

<b>Appoint Aharon and his sons.</b> The word connotes appointment, not counting. 
<b>And they shall guard their priesthood.</b> Referring to the blood [of the sacrificial offerings], sprinkling [it on the altar], burning [the sacrifices], [and other] services entrusted to the <i>kohanim.</i> 

Verse 11



Verse 12

<b>Behold, I have taken [the Levites].</b> What is My right to them? <b>From among Bnei Yisroel</b> That the Israelites must hire them to serve Me? Through the [Israelites’] first born, I gained my right to them, having taken them (the Levites) in their place. Because the sacred service was [originally performed] by the firstborn, but when they sinned with the golden calf, they were disqualified. The Levites, who did not indulge in idolatry, were chosen instead. 

Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15

<b>From the age of one month and above.</b> When he (the infant) can no longer be categorized as stillborn, he is listed among those entitled “guardian of the sacred watch.” R’ Yehudah B’rabi Shalom said, “This [Levite] tribe is regularly counted from the womb, as it is said, “. . . [Yocheved, Levi’s daughter] . . . whom she (Levi’s wife) bore to Levi in Egypt . . .” While entering the portals of Egypt, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>she bore her (Yocheved). yet she is counted among the seventy souls [who came down to Egypt]. for, when one tallies their total, one finds only sixty-nine and she completed the total. 

Verse 16

<b>According to the word of Adonoy.</b> Moshe said before the Holy One, Blessed is He, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”How can I enter into their tents to determine the number of their nursing infants”? The Holy One, Blessed is He, replied, “Do yours, and I will do Mine”! Moshe proceeded, and stood at the door of the tent, whereupon the Divine Presence preceded him [and entered the tent]. A voice then echoed from the tent, announcing, “There are so many and so many nursing infants in this tent”! This is why it is said, “. . . according to the word of God . . .” 


Verse 17



Verse 18



Verse 19



Verse 20



Verse 21

<b>Of Gershon, the family of Livni.</b> Meaning, of Gershon, those who were counted [was] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the family of Livni and the family of Shim’i — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>their numbers were so many and so many. 


Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24



Verse 25

<b>The Mishkon.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The lower [ceiling] drapes.
<b>And the Tent.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The goats’ hair drapes, made [to serve] as the roof. 
<b>Its Cover.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Ram skins and <i>tachash</i> skins. 

<b>And the curtain for the entrance</b> This is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the drape.

Verse 26

<b>And its ropes.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Of the <i>Mishkon</i> and the tent, but not the enclosure. 

Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29

<b>The families of the children of Kehos shall camp . . . on the south.</b> Near them [was] the banner of Reuven, who camped to the south. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Woe to the wicked, woe to his neighbor! This is why [Reuven’s constituents] were punished — Doson, Avirom, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and two hundred and fifty men — together with Korach and his assembly, because they (the Reuvenites) were drawn, with them, into the dispute. 

Verse 30



Verse 31

<b>And the curtain.</b> This is the <i>Paroches,</i> as it was also called “. . . the <i>Paroches</i> screen . . .” 


Verse 32

<b>The leader of the leaders of Levi.</b> [He was] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>appointed over all of them. Over what was his leadership?
<b>The appointment of the guardians to safeguard — </b> They were all appointed by him. 


Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36



Verse 37



Verse 38

<b>Moshe, Aharon and his sons.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Near them [was] the banner of the camp of Yehudah, and those who camped near him, Yissachar and Zevulun. Good fortune to the righteous, good fortune to his neighbor! Because they were neighbors of Moshe, who engaged in Torah [study], they became great Torah scholars, as it is said, “Yehudah my lawgiver”; “From the sons of Yissachar of sagacious knowledge, etc.” — [this refers to] two hundred heads of Sanhedrin; “and from Zevulun, came those that handle the scribe’s quill.” 

Verse 39

<b>Whom Moshe and Aharon counted.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>There are dots over [the word] וְאַהֲרֹן, to teach that he was not included in the counting of the Levites. 
<b>Twenty two thousand.</b> When counting them individually, however, one discovers three hundred extra: the sons of Gershon, seven thousand five hundred; the sons of Kehos, eight thousand six hundred; the sons of Merori, six thousand two hundred [hence, twenty two thousand three hundred]. Why aren’t they included among the rest to redeem the firstborn, thus exempting the two hundred seventy three overlapping firstborn from redemption? Our sages answered, in Maseches Bechoros, that the three hundred Levites were, themselves, firstborn. It was sufficient <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for them to release themselves from redemption. 

Verse 40

<b>Count every male firstborn . . . from the age of one month and above.</b> When he (the infant) can no longer be categorized as stillborn. 


Verse 41



Verse 42



Verse 43



Verse 44



Verse 45

<b>And the animals of the Levites . . .etc.</b> The animals of the Levites did not redeem the firstlings of the Israelites’ clean (i.e., kosher) animals, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but [they did redeem] the firstlings of their donkeys. And a single sheep belonging to a Levite released numerous of the Israelites’ donkey firstlings. The proof is that Scripture counts the extra men, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but did not count the extra animals. 

Verse 46

<b>And the redemption of the [two hundred and seventy-]three.</b> The firstborn who require redemption among them (the Israelites), these are the two hundred seventy-three extras among them, over and above the Levites. From them, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>take five <i>shekolim</i> per head. This was the sale price for Yoseif, twenty silver [pieces], who was Rochel’s firstborn. 


Verse 47



Verse 48



Verse 49

<b>[Those whose numbers were] in excess of those who were redeemed through the Levites.</b> Those redeemed by the very presence of the Levites.

Verse 50

<b>One thousand three hundred sixty five.</b> This is the sum total, [at] five <i>shekolim</i> per head. For two hundred firstborn: one thousand <i>shekolim.</i> For seventy firstborn — three hundred and fifty <i>shekolim.</i> For three firstborn — fifteen <i>shekolim.</i> He (Moshe) said, “How shall I do this? Any firstborn whom I tell to pay five <i>shekolim</i> will say, ‘I am from those redeemed by the Levites”’! What did he do? He brought <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>twenty-two thousand slips and wrote “Levite” on them, and two hundred and seventy three slips and wrote “five <i>shekolim</i>” on them. He mixed them together, and placed them in a container. [Then] he told them, “Come, choose your slips by lot.” 


Chapter 4



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>Take the count . . . etc.</b> Count those among them suited <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for the service of carrying, the ones from thirty to fifty years of age. Someone younger than thirty, has not reached prime strength. From here they (the Rabbis) derive “[the age of] thirty for strength” and after fifty, one’s strength diminishes. 


Verse 3



Verse 4

<b>The Holy of Holies.</b> The Holiest of all; the Ark, the Table, the Menorah, the Altars, the Paroches, and the service vessels. 

Verse 5

<b>Aharon and his sons shall enter . . . etc.</b> They shall place each vessel into the sheath specified for it in this chapter, so that the Levite sons of Kehos need do nothing but carry [them]. 
<b>When the camp is about to travel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When the cloud rises, they know that they are to depart. 


Verse 6



Verse 7

<b>Molds, spoons, rods, covering props.</b> I have explained this in [the chapter dealing with] the work of the <i>Mishkon.</i> 
<b>Covering.</b> Covering, from the word מָסָךְ, cover, as it is written, “. . . by which they (the breads) shall be covered.” 

Verse 8



Verse 9

<b>Its tongs.</b> A type of pliers with which they pull the wick in any desired direction.
<b>Its scoops.</b> A type of small spoon with a flat, uncurved bottom, unwalled at the front — only at the sides, with which he rakes the ashes from the lamps when cleaning them. 
<b>It lamps.</b> <i>Loces,</i> lamps, in Old French, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in which the oil and wicks are placed. 


Verse 10

<b>Into the covering of the tachash — hide.</b> A type of <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>sack.

Verse 11



Verse 12

<b>All the service utensils with which they serve in the Sanctuary.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Inside the <i>Mishkon,</i> which is Holy. These are the incense vessels, with which they serve on the inner altar. 


Verse 13

<b>They shall remove the ashes from the Altar. </b> The copper altar.
<b>They shall remove the ashes.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They shall take the ashes away from it.
<b>And spread upon it a cloth of purple [wool].</b> The fire which descended from heaven lay below the cloth <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>like a lion when they traveled. It didn’t burn it (the cloth), because they arched a copper <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>vessel over it. 

Verse 14

<b>Firepans.</b> With these they raked the coals for the lifting of the ashes. This was made like a pan with only three sides, and the front was used to draw the coals. 
<b>Forks.</b> Copper hooks with which they prodded the limbs on the altar, turning them so that they would be completely consumed quickly. 
<b>Scoops.</b> These were scrapers, In Old French, <i>Wadil,</i> scoops. They were made of copper, and used to sweep the ashes from the Altar. 

Verse 15

<b>Covering of the Sanctuary.</b> The Ark and the Altar.
<b>And all of the holy utensils.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The Menorah and the service vessels.
<b>And they will [not] die.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Since, if they touch, they will be subject to death by Heavenly decree. 

Verse 16

<b>Encharged to Elazar.</b> He was assigned <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to carry them; oil, incense, and anointing oil. The continual [daily] meal-offering. His responsibility was to issue orders, to urge [the others], and to offer it [on the altar] when they camped. 

<b>The charge of the entire Mishkon.</b> In addition, he was assigned to [oversee] the load of the sons of Kehos — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to issue orders for everyone’s work and load. This is [what is meant by] “the <i>Mishkon and all of its contents,” everything listed above in this chapter. But the load of the sons of Gershon and Merori, which did not consist of the holy of holies, was by order of Isamar, as is written in the portion of נָשׂא . 
</i>

Verse 17



Verse 18

<b>Do not cut off.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Do not cause them to die.

Verse 19



Verse 20

<b>They shall not come in to see when the holy is being covered.</b> [When placed] into its sheath, as specified above in this chapter, they shall spread over it a certain cloth, they shall cover it with a certain cover. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Its “ בִּלּוּעַ “ refers to the covering of it. 


Verse 21



Verse 22

<b>Take the count of the sons of Gershon, as well.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Just as I commanded you conce ning the sons of Kehos, to determine how many <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>have reached the working category. 

Verse 23



Verse 24



Verse 25

<b>The tapestries of the Mishkon.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The ten lower ones.
<b>And the Tent of Meeting.</b> The <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>goat-hair tapestries, made as a tent over it (the <i>Mishkon</i>). 
<b>Its covering.</b> The <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>red dyed rams’ skins.
<b>The screen for the entrance.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The eastern curtain. 


Verse 26

<b>Which are over the Mishkon.</b> As if it had said, “The curtains and screen of the courtyard enclosure which protect and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>guard over the <i>Mishkon 
and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the copper altar on all sides.” 
</i>
<b>And all that will be given [lit. made] to them.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] translates, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”all that will be given to them” — to the sons of Gershon. 

Verse 27

<b>By instruction of Aharon and [one of] his sons.</b> Which of his sons is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>appointed over them? Under the supervision of Isamar, son of Aharon, the <i>kohein.</i> 


Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32

<b>Their stakes and ropes.</b> Of the pillars, since the the stakes and ropes of the curtains were in the load of the sons of Gershon. There were stakes and ropes at the bottom of the tapestries and curtains, so that the wind would not lift them; and there were stakes <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and ropes for the pillars, on all sides, from which to hang the curtains, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>by their upper border, with bars <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and rods, as is taught in [the Beraysa of] the work of the <i>Mishkon.</i> 
 

Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36



Verse 37



Verse 38



Verse 39



Verse 40



Verse 41



Verse 42



Verse 43



Verse 44



Verse 45



Verse 46



Verse 47

<b>The service of service.</b> This refers to the song of the cymbals and the harps, which is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>service for [another] service. 
<b>And the service of carrying.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As the phrase indicates.

Verse 48



Verse 49

<b>And they were counted, as Adonoy commanded Moshe.</b> Those counted were, as commanded, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>from the ages of thirty to fifty. 


Chapter 5



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>Command Bnei Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This <i>parshah</i> was said on the day the <i>Mishkon</i> was erected. Eight <i>parshiyos</i> were said on that day, as is stated in Tractate Gittin, <i>perek</i> Hanizakin. 
<b>They must expel from the camp.</b> There were <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>three camps when they rested: Within the curtains was the camp of the <i>Shechinah;</i> the surrounding Levite encampment, as stated expressly in the <i>parshah</i> of Bemidbar Sinai, was the camp of the Levites; from there to the end of the encampment of the banners, in all the four directions, was the camp of the Israelites. The <i>metzoro</i> was sent <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>out of all of them. The <i>zav</i> was permitted in the camp of the Israelites, but expelled from the [other] two. A person defiled by the dead was permitted even among the [encampment of] the Levites, being expelled only <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>from the encampment of the <i>Shechinah.</i> All this, the Rabbis derive from Scriptural passages in Maseches Pesachim. 
<b>Defiled by a [departed] soul.</b> [Onkelos renders] דִּמְסָאָב לִטְמֵי נַפְשָׁא דֶאֱנָשָׁא, (“who were defiled by the bones of a human soul.”) In my opinion, the word <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>means “human bones” in Aramaic. There are many [examples] in Bereishis Rabbah, “ טַמְיָא “ אַדְרִיאָנוּס שְׁחִיק — may [his] “bones” be crushed. 


Verse 3



Verse 4



Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>Acting treacherously against Adonoy.</b> Scripture now reiterates the <i>parshah</i> of the thief who swears falsely, previously stated in the Portion of Vayikra, “[If a person sins] . . . and acts treacherously against God, lying to his fellow . . .” It is repeated here for the sake of two innovations. Firstly, Scripture writes “And they confess . . . [their sin],” teaching that he (the thief) is not required to pay the fifth and bring the <i>asham</i> (guilt-offering) when convicted by the testimony of witnesses, unless he confesses to the act. And secondly, [to teach] that property stolen from a proselyte must be given to the <i>kohanim.</i> 

Verse 7

<b>Principal amount of his guilt.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is the principal [payment] concerning which he took the oath.
<b>To whom he is indebted.</b> To the one <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to whom he is liable.

Verse 8

<b>But if the man has no redeemer.</b> As the claimant died who put him (the thief) to the oath — without heirs.
<b>To whom the debt may be returned.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When he (the thief) recants and confesses to his crime. The Rabbis remark, ‘Is there anyone in Yisroel without redeemers, whether a son, brother, or paternal blood relation [branching] upward to [the patriarch] Yaakov? But <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>[this refers to] a proselyte who died without heirs. 
<b>The debt being returned.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is the principal and the fifth thereof.
<b>To Adonoy, [then] to the kohein.</b> God takes possession of it, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>then gives it to the <i>kohein [serving] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in that watch. </i>
<b>Besides the ram of forgiveness.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Mentioned in Vayikra, which he is required to bring. 

Verse 9

<b>Every terumah-gift, etc.</b> R’ Yishmael said, “Is <i>terumah</i>-gift brought to the <i>kohein</i>? Does he not seek it, himself, in the granary? Then why does the Torah state, ‘ . . . which they bring to the <i>kohein</i>?’ These are the <i>bikurim</i>-gifts, about which it is stated, ‘[. . . the first fruits of your land] must be brought to the House of Adonoy, your God.’ <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But one does not know what must be done with them. The Torah therefore states, ‘ . . . to the <i>kohein,</i> it shall belong to him.’ Scripture teaches, concerning the <i>bikurim</i>-gifts, that they must be given to the <i>kohein.</i> 

Verse 10

<b>A man’s sacred objects shall be his.</b> Since the priestly and Levite gifts are mandated, one might assume that they may confiscate them forcefully. The Torah therefore teaches that “A man’s sacred objects shall be his,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>informing [us] that the executory benefits belong to the [original Israelite] owner. Many other homiletical interpretations are offered by Sifri. Midrash Aggadah [states], “A man’s sacred objects shall be his” [states]: If someone withholds his tithes, and refuses to give them, [then] “[they shall] be his” — the tithes. Ultimately, his land will yield only one tenth of its normal produce. 

<b>Whatever a man gives to the kohein [lit. A man who gives to the <i>kohein].</i></b><i> The proper gifts. </i>
<b>Shall be his.</b> Great riches.

Verse 11



Verse 12

<b>If any man’s wife goes astray.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>What is written [immediately] above this subject? “A man’s sacred objects shall be his.” (v. 10) [This implies that] If you withhold the <i>kohein’s</i> gifts, then by your life! You will find it necessary to visit him, to bring the <i>sotah</i> to him. 
<b>Any man [lit. A man, a man].</b> This teaches that she is doubly treacherous; against the “man of warfare” on high, and her husband [lit. “man”] below. 
<b>[If any man’s] wife goes astray.</b> Our Rabbis teach: Adulterers do not commit adultery unless they are imbued with the <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>spirit of foolishness, as it is written כִּי תִשְׂטֶה [lit. acts foolishly]. and it is written, “the adulterer lacks reason”: The simple explanation of the verse is, “[If any man’s wife] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>turns aside from the ways of modesty” and arouses his suspicion, as in “turn aside from him, and pass by,” “let your heart not turn to her ways. 
<b>And acts treacherously toward him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>What is the treachery? 


Verse 13

<b>And a man has lain.</b> This excludes a minor and a non-human.
<b>With her.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Lying with her disqualifies her. but not laying with her sister (as in the incident of two sisters who resembled one another). 

<b>But it was hidden from her husband’s eyes.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This excludes a blind man. Therefore, if he (the husband) saw [the adultery] and feigned ignorance, the [bitter] waters do not test her. 
<b>She was concealed.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Long enough to have been defiled by intercourse.
<b>There is no witness against her.</b> But if <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>even one witness testified that she was defiled [by intercourse], she did not drink [the bitter waters]. 
<b>There is no witness against her.</b> To the defilement, but there are witnesses to the concealment. 
<b>Seized forcibly.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Ravished, as in, “. . . siezed her forcibly and laid with her.” 

Verse 14

<b>Comes upon him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Before the concealment.
<b>A spirit of jealousy, and he is jealous.</b> The Rabbis interpret this as “warning.” He warns her not to be alone with a certain man, 
<b>And she was defiled. Or, comes upon him . . . etc.</b> As if it had said, ‘he warned her and she ignored the warning, but <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>it is not known whether or not she was defiled.’ 

Verse 15

<b>flour.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But not of fine flour.
<b>Barley.</b> But not wheat. [Because] she acted like an animal, her offering consists of animal feed. 
<b>He shall not pour oil over it.</b> So that her offering may not be resplendent. for, [olive] oil is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>identified as light, while she acted in darkness. 
<b>He shall not put frankincense on it.</b> The matriarchs are called “frankincense,” as it is said, “. . . and to the hill of frankincense,” but she departed from their ways. 
<b>For it is a meal-offering of jealousy.</b> This meal. “Meal” is masculine.
<b>A meal-offering of jealousy (wrath).</b> She arouses a double wrath against her; the wrath of the Supreme Omnipresent Being, and the wrath of her husband. 

Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>Sanctified waters.</b> Sanctified in the wash basin. Because the wash basin was made from the copper of the “multitude mirrors,” while this [<i>sotah</i>] departed from their ways. They had relations with their husbands in Egypt beneath the apple tree, but this [<i>sotah</i>] corrupted herself with a stranger — let her be tested by it (the wash basin). 
<b>In a clay utensil.</b> She served the adulterer excellent wine in superb goblets — therefore, let her drink the bitter water in a wretched clay cup. 

Verse 18

<b>The kohein shall station . . . etc., </b> Has it not already said, ‘ . .and station her before Adonoy’? (V. 16) <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But, they moved her from place to place to exhaust her, so that she might lose her composure and confess. 
<b>Expose.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He disentangles the plaits of her hair, to humiliate her. From this we derive that, for daughters of Yisroel, a bared head is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>debasing. 
<b>Before Adonoy.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>At the <i>Nikanor</i> gate. This was the eastern gateway to the [Temple] courtyard, the route by which everyone entered. 
<b>And place, on her palms.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To exhaust her, [in the hope] that she might lose her composure and confess, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>so that the Sacred Name not be erased in the water. 
<b>The bitter.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because of their aftermath, when they are bitter to her. 
<b>Lethal.</b> Which eliminate her from the world, like the phrase, “. . . lethal thornbush.” But it is inappropriate to translate “accursed waters,” as they are sacred [v.17]. And Scripture does not write אֲרוּרִים, but מְאָרְרִים — affecting others. Even Onkelos did not translate לִיטַיָּא, “accursed,” but מְלַטְטַיָּא, “curse causing” — they reveal the curse in the body of this [<i>sotah</i>]. 

Verse 19

<b>Shall place her under oath . . . etc. </b> What is the oath? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>‘If no [man] laid [with you], be absolved but if he laid [with you], may you choke’! A negative statement expresses, by implication, its positive converse, but we are commanded to open capital cases with the presumption of innocence. 

Verse 20

<b>If you have gone astray.</b> כִּי is used <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in the sense of “if.”

Verse 21

<b>With the oath of accursedness.</b> The oath which contains the curse.
<b>Adonoy shall make you a curse:</b> Everyone will curse through you: ‘May [a curse] befall you <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the way it befell so-and-so.’
<b>And an oath.</b> Everyone will swear through you: ‘If [my oath is] not [true], may [disaster] happen to me the way it happened to so-and-so. Similarly, it says, “you will leave your names [to be used] as an oath by My chosen.” — the virtuous swear by the punishment of the wicked. Similarly, with regard to blessings, “and through you will be blessed . . . etc., “through you shall [the People of] Yisroel bless, saying. . .” 
<b>Your thigh.</b> In the curse, the thigh precedes the abdomen, because her transgression began there. 
<b>Swell.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] translates, “swollen.” 


Verse 22

<b>To swell the abdomen.</b> [לַצְבּוֹת בֶּטֶן is] like לְהַצְבּוֹת בֶּטֶן, “to cause the abdomen to swell.” This is the function of the פַּתַּח when it vocalizes the ל' . Similarly, לַנְחוֹתָם הַדֶּרֶךְ, (“to lead them on the way,”) לַרְאוֹתְכֶם בַּדֶּרֶךְ אֲשֶר תֵּלְכוּ בָהּ (“to show you the way in which to go.”) Similarly, לַנְפִּל יָרֵך, לְהַנְפִּיל יָרֵךְ (“to cause the thigh to collapse”). The waters swell the abdomen and collapse the thigh. 
<b>To swell the abdomen and collapse the thigh.</b> The abdomen and thigh of the adulterer, or perhaps it refers only to the adulteress? When Scripture says, “. . . your thigh to collapse and abdomen to swell,” the [punishment of the] adulteress has been stated. 
<b>Amein, Amein.</b> [This is] The acceptance of the oath. Amein <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for the curse, Amein for the oath. Amein if [I strayed] from this husband, Amein if [I strayed] from a different husband. Amein that I did not stray [when] betrothed, married, levirately engaged or taken to his home. 


Verse 23



Verse 24

<b>He shall have the woman drink.</b> It was not done in this order, as <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he brought her offering first. But Scripture informs you that when he does give her the waters, they will penetrate her with bitterness. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Since it [merely] says “abdomen” and “thigh,” how do we know the rest of the body [is affected]? The Torah states “and [the waters] shall enter her,” completely. If so, why does the Torah say “abdomen” and “thigh”? Since they began the transgression, the punishment began with them. 
<b>To become bitter.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They will be harmful and bitter for her. 


Verse 25

<b>And shall wave.</b> He moves it forward, back, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>up, and down. She, too, waves with him, with her hand <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>above the hand of the <i>kohein.</i> 
<b>And bring it.</b> This refers to placing it at the southwest corner of the altar <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>before taking the handful, like the other <i>minchah</i>- offerings. 

Verse 26

<b>Its commemoration.</b> This is the handful. Through its burning, the <i>mincha</i>-offering is remembered on high. (Sifri, 5:72.) 

Verse 27

<b>He shall make her drink the water.</b> [This is written] to add that if she said, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”I will not drink” after the scroll was erased, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>we coerce her, forcing her to drink against her will, unless she says “I am defiled.” 
<b>Her abdomen will swell.</b> Although, in the curse, Scripture mentions the thigh first, the water <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>tested her just the way it entered her. 
<b>The woman will be a curse.</b> As I explained, everyone will <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>use her to curse. 
<b>Among her people.</b> There is a difference between a person disgraced <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>among those who know her, and a person disgraced among those who do not know her. 

Verse 28

<b>But if the woman was not defiled.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>During this concealment.
<b>And is pure.</b> From any other place.
<b>She will be cleansed.</b> Of the lethal waters. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Furthermore, “she will bear seed” — if she suffered during childbirth, her labor will now be painless. If she gave birth to swarthy [babies], they will now be light. 

Verse 29



Verse 30

<b>If (lit., or) [he is] a man.</b> As in, “If it was known.” As if it had said, “If he is a vengeful man, and, therefore, he shall have the woman stand.” 


Verse 31

<b>The man is cleansed of sin.</b> If the water affected her, let him not be tormented saying: “I was responsible for her death.” He is cleansed from punishment. Another interpretation: After he (the <i>kohein</i>) causes her to drink, she is permitted to be with him (her husband), and he is cleansed of sin. For, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the [untested] <i>sotah</i> is forbidden to [have intimate relations with] her husband. 

Chapter 6



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>If . . . sets apart.</b> Sets [himself] apart. Why is the chapter of the nazirite placed next to the chapter of the <i>sotah</i>? To tell you <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that whoever observes a <i>sotah</i> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in her decadence should take the <i>nazirite</i> vow against wine, which leads to promiscuity. 
<b>A nazirite vow.</b> נְזִירָה always indicates abstinence. Here, too, he abstains from wine. 
<b>To set [himself] apart for Adonoy.</b> To separate himself from wine for the sake of heaven.

Verse 3

<b>From new or old [intoxicating] wine.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] translates; “from new wine or old”: <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Wine intoxicates when aged.
<b>Anything steeped in grapes.</b> The word [מִשְׁרַת] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>denotes adding color to water, or any beverage. In the Mishnaic idiom, there are many [examples]: ‘One does not steep ink or dye’, ‘If a nazirite steeped his bread in wine’. 

Verse 4

<b>Seeds.</b> These are the kernels.
<b>Skin.</b> These are the outer shells in which the seeds are [held] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>like the tongue of a bell. 


Verse 5

<b>He shall be sacred.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>His hair, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for growing the growth of hair on his head. 
<b>Long.</b> This is vocalized with <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>a <i>small patach</i> (<i>segol</i>), even though it is attached to “the hair of his head” — the growth of hair. The meaning of פֶּרַע is “growth of hair.” Similarly, “He (the <i>kohein gadol</i>) shall not permit the growth of hair on his head.” It is not considered a פֶּרַע (growth) [if uncut] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>less than thirty days. 


Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8

<b>All the days of his separation, he is sacred.</b> This refers to personal sanctity, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>from defilement [by contact] with the dead. 

Verse 9

<b>Suddenly.</b> This refers to the unavoidable.
<b>[Or] unexpectedly.</b> This refers to the unintentional. Some say פֶּתַע פִּתְאוֹם is a single statement, [meaning] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”a sudden incident.” 
<b>If someone died near him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>In the tent where he was.
<b>On the day of his purification.</b> On the day <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>when he is sprinkled. Or, perhaps only the eighth [day], when he is completely purified? The Torah therefore states, “on the seventh day.” If the seventh, perhaps even if he was not sprinkled? The Torah therefore states, “on the day of his purification.” 

Verse 10

<b>On the eighth day he shall take two turtledoves.</b> This excludes the seventh [day]. Or perhaps it is intended to exclude the ninth [day]? [Scripture] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>designated a time for the offerings, and designated a time for those who bring them. Just as the offerings are sanctioned on the eighth, and from the eighth and onward, so [are] those who bring them [sanctioned] on the eighth, and from the eighth and onward. 

Verse 11

<b>From his sin [of contact] with a [departed] soul.</b> He was negligent about defilement with the dead. R’ Elazar Hakapar says, [the sin was] that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he inflicted suffering on himself by abstaining from wine. 
<b>He shall sanctify his head.</b> By beginning, again, his nazirite counting. 


Verse 12

<b>He shall set apart, for Adonoy, his nazarite days.</b> He shall repeat the count of his nazarite days as [counted] originally. 
<b>The first days shall elapse.</b> Be discounted.

Verse 13

<b>He shall bring himself [lit. him].</b> He shall bring himself. This is one of the three usages of אֶת, (literally, “him”), which R’ Yishmael explained this way. Similarly, “They will burden them with sin and guilt. — themselves.” Similarly, “He (Moshe) buried אוֹתוֹ (lit. him) in the valley.” He buried himself. 

Verse 14



Verse 15

<b>And their meal-offerings and libations.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Of the burnt-offering and the peace- offering. Because they were included in a group, but then distinguished innovatively, requiring bread, Scripture reinstates them into the group, [stating] that they require libations, following the rule of all burnt and peace-offerings. 
<b>Matzoh loaves [mixed with oil] and matzoh wafers.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Ten of each kind.

Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>A peace-offering for Adonoy, along with the basket of matzos.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He shall slaughter the peace-offering with the intent to sanctify the bread. 
<b>His meal-offering and libation.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The ram’s.

Verse 18

<b>The Nazir shall shave at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting.</b> Perhaps he shaves in the courtyard? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But this would be grossly disrepectful. Rather, the <i>Nazir</i> shall shave <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>after the slaughter of the <i>shelamim</i>, concerning which is written “. . . and slaughter, it [the peace-offering] at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting.” 
<b>Which is under the peace-offering sacrifice.</b> Underneath <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the pot in which he cooks it. Because the <i>Nazir’s</i> peace-offerings <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>were cooked in the courtyard, since the <i>kohein</i> had to remove the foreleg after it was cooked and wave it before God. 

Verse 19

<b>The cooked foreleg.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>After it was cooked.

Verse 20

<b>It is consecrated to the kohein.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The loaf, wafer, and foreleg are <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i><i>terumah</i>-gifts to the <i>kohein. </i>
<b>Besides the breast of the wave-offering.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Besides the breast and the shoulder that are due to him from all peace-offerings, there is added to the nazirite peace-offerings, this foreleg. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because the nazirite peace-offerings were included in a group, but then distinguished innovatively, for the consecration of the foreleg, Scripture must reinstate them into the group and deal, also, with the breast and shoulder. 


Verse 21

<b>Aside from what he can afford to bring.</b> If he said, “I am hereby a <i>Nazir</i> with the stipulation to shave [my hair] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>relative to a hundred burnt-offerings and a hundred peace-offerings,” [his vow is effective]. According to his vow, that he vows, so shall he fulfill. Added . . . Beyond his nazirite laws. Beyond the nazirite laws. He may <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>increase, but not reduce. If he said, “I am hereby a nazirite five times [consecutively], with the stipulation to shave [my hair] relative to these three animals,” I do not read, concerning him, “whatever he vows, so shall he do.” 


Verse 22



Verse 23

<b>Saying.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like זָכוֹר, “remembering,” שָׁמוֹר, “keeping.” in Old French, “<i>disant</i>” — gerund. 
<b>Saying to them.</b> So that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they all hear.
<b>Saying.</b> [אָמוֹר is] Full. Do not bless them with haste and rushing, but with concentration and a whole heart. 

Verse 24

<b>May . . . bless you.</b> May your possessions be blessed.
<b>And protect you.</b> From thieves descending on you for your money. A person who presents a gift to his servant is unable to protect him from everybody, so if bandits descend on him and take it from him, what benefit does he have from the gift? But the Holy One, Blessed is He, is both giver and protector. There are many homiletic interpretations in Sifri. 

Verse 25

<b>May Adonoy cause His countenance to shine upon you.</b> May he show you a joyous, radiant countenance. 
<b>And favor you.</b> May he grant you favor.

Verse 26

<b>May Adonoy lift his face to you.</b> May he subdue his anger.

Verse 27

<b>They shall bestow My Name.</b> They shall bless them with the explicit Name [of God]. 

<b>And I will bless them.</b> The Israelites. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I will concur with [the blessing of] the <i>kohanim.</i> Another interpretation [of] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”And I will bless them” — The <i>kohanim.</i>

Chapter 7



Verse 1

<b>It came to pass, on the day Moshe finished.</b> The text reads כַּלּוֹת . On the day that the <i>Mishkon</i> was erected, the Israelites were like a כַּלָּה — a bride entering the wedding canopy. 
<b>Moshe finished.</b> Bezalel, Aholiav, and all the wise — hearted men constructed the <i>Mishkon,</i> yet Scripture credits it to Moshe, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>because he utterly dedicated himself to it, observing the structural design of each object as shown to him on the mountain (Sinai) in order to instruct the artisans, without making a single error in design. We find a similarity with regard to [king] David, because he utterly dedicated himself to the construction of the Beis Ha Mikdash — as it is said: “Remember, Adonoy, unto David all his afflictions; how he swore to Adonoy . . . etc. it was, therefore, called by his name, as it is said: “Observe your House, David.” 
<b>[On the day] Moshe finished erecting.</b> It does not say, “On the day [Moshe] erected . . .” This teaches that throughout the seven days of installation Moshe erected and dismantled it, and on that day, he erected it without dismantling it. This is why it says, “On the day Moshe finished erecting” — that day his erecting ended. It was the first of the month of Nisan. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>On the second, the [red] cow was burned, on the third, they sprinkled with the first sprinkling, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and on the seventh, [after having been sprinkled again] they were shaven. 


Verse 2

<b>They were the leaders of the tribes.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They were officers over them in Egypt, and were beaten because of them, as it is said: “And the officers of the Israelites were beaten, etc.” 
<b>They stood by during the counting.</b> They stood with Moshe and Aharon when they counted [Bnei] Yisroel, as it is said, “with you [Moshe and Aharon], shall be. . .” 

Verse 3

<b>Six covered wagons.</b> צָב can only mean “covered.” Similarly, “[They will bring your brothers from all the nations . . . with horses and chariots] וּבַצַּבִּים וּבַפְּרָדִים,” “in covered wagons and on mules . . .” Covered wagons are called צַבִּים . [Some interpret צָב in the sense of הַצְבִי יִשְׂרָאֵל, (“The finest in Israel.”) They (the wagons) were fine looking.] 
<b>They placed them before the Mishkon.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because Moshe did not accept [the gift] from their hands until [so] instructed by the omnipresent [God.] R’ Noson said, “Why did the leaders see fit to contribute here at the outset, but for the materials of the <i>Mishkon,</i> they did not contribute at the outset? Because the leaders said as follows: “Let the community contribute as they wish, and any shortfall, we will furnish.” But when they saw that the community had supplied everything, as it is said, “the material was sufficient,” they said, “Now what can we do”? They brought the onyx stones, and the stones set into the <i>ephod and breastplate. This is why they contributed here at the outset. </i>

Verse 4



Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7

<b>According to their work.</b> The load of the sons of Gershon was lighter than that of the sons of Merori, who carried the planks, pillars, and sockets. 


Verse 8



Verse 9

<b>Because the sacred work was [incumbent] on them.</b> The carrying of sacred objects — the ark, table, etc. Therefore, “they had to carry [them] on their shoulders.” 

Verse 10

<b>The leaders brought forward the [offerings for] the consecration of the altar.</b> After they contributed the wagons and cattle to carry the <i>Mishkon,</i> they were ennobled to contribute the offerings for the altar to consecrate it. 
<b>The leaders placed their offering before the altar.</b> Because <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Moshe did not accept [the gift] from their hands until [so] instructed by the Almighty. 


Verse 11

<b>They shall bring forth their offering for the dedication of the altar.</b> But Moshe still did not know how they were to bring the offerings — whether in order of their birth, or in order of the traveling — until the Holy One, Blessed is He, told him that they should bring the offerings according to the traveling, each in his day. 

Verse 12

<b>On the first day.</b> That day took ten crowns; [it fell on] the first [day] of creation, first of the leaders, etc., as recorded in Seder Olam. 
<b>Of the tribe of Yehudah.</b> Scripture establishes his tribal kinship; <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but not that he solicited [payment] from his tribe and then brought [the offering]. But perhaps I should say לְמַטֵּה יְהוּדָה, “for the tribe of Yehudah,” [teaching] that he solicited payment from his tribe and then brought [the offering]? The Torah therefore teaches “this is Nachshon’s offering.” He brought his own. 

Verse 13

<b>Both were filled with fine flour.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As a voluntary meal-offering.

Verse 14

<b>[Of] ten gold [<i>shekolim</i>].</b> As Targum [Onkelos] interprets, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the weight of ten <i>shekolim</i> by the Sanctuary standard was in it. 
<b>Filled with incense.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>We do not find incense [brought] by an individual, nor [brought] on the outer altar, except for this one alone. This was a temporary injunction. 

Verse 15

<b>One [young] bull.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The best of its herd. 


Verse 16

<b>One he-goat as a sin-offering.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To atone for [defilement by passing over] the grave of the abyss — [for] indefinite defilement.

Verse 17



Verse 18

<b>Nesanel the son of Tzu’ar brought forward — he brought forward his offering.</b> What does the Torah teach [by saying] “he brought forward” with respect to the tribe of Yissachar, without having said it with respect to all the [other] tribes? Because Reuven came with a complaint, saying ‘Enough that Yehudah preceded me! Let me bring my offering after him.’ Moshe said to him, By the Almighty ‘It was told to me that they should bring the offerings in the order of the journeys, according to their banners.’ This is why it says אֶת קָרְבָּנוֹ “ הִקְרִב,” without the “<i>yud</i>,” inferring הַקְרֵב, “you shall bring forward!” — the imperative usage, since Moshe was commanded by the Almighty, “ הַקְרֵב .” What is [the inference of] “[Nesanel] brought forward,” [“he brought forward”] twice? Because there were two reasons by which he merited bringing his offering second among the tribes. One, because of their (his tribe’s) knowledge of Torah, as it is said, “From the sons of Yissachar, of sagacious, timely knowledge.” And one, because they advised the leaders to donate these offerings. In R’ Moshe Hadarshan’s commentary I found: “R’ Pinchos ben Yair said: ‘Nesanel the son of Tzu'ar offered this advice.”’ 

Verse 19

<b>Silver tray.</b> Its letters are numerically equivalent to <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>930, corresponding to the years of Adam. 

<b>Its weight was one hundred thirty [<i>shekolim</i>].</b> Alluding that when he (Adam) fathered progeny to sustain the world, he was one hundred thirty years old, as it is said: “Adam lived one hundred thirty years, and fathered . . . etc.” 
<b>One silver bowl.</b> The numerical value is 520, alluding to Noach, who fathered his progeny at the age of 500, and alluding to the 20 years by which the decree for the flood preceded his progeny, as I explained [the verse] “His days shall be a hundred and twenty years.” This is why it says מִזְרָק אֶחָד כֶּסֶף, but does not say מִזְרַק כֶּסֶף אֶחָד, as it says concerning the tray — to teach that the letters of אֶחָד are also included in the calculation. 
<b>Seventy shekolim.</b> Corresponding to the 70 nations which emerged from his (Noach’s) sons.

Verse 20

<b>One spoon (lit. hand).</b> Corresponding to the Torah, which was given from the hand of the Holy One, Blessed is He. 
<b>Ten gold [shekolim].</b> Corresponding to the ten commandments.
<b>Filled with incense.</b> The numerical value of קְטֹרֶת, is 613, corresponding to the 613 commandments — provided you convert the קו"ף into a דל"ת, by using א"ת ב"ש ג"ר ד"ק . 


Verse 21

<b>One [young] bull.</b> Corresponding to Avraham, concerning whom it is said: “He took a young bull.” 
<b>One ram.</b> Corresponding to Yitzchok, “He took the ram.” 
<b>One [yearling] sheep.</b> Corresponding to Yaakov: “Yaakov separated the sheep.”

Verse 22

<b>Goat.</b> To atone for the sale of Yoseif, concerning whom it is said: “They slaughtered a goat.” 

Verse 23

<b>For the peace-offering sacrifice, two oxen.</b> Corresponding to Moshe and Aharon, who made peace between the Israelites and their Father in heaven. 
<b>Rams, goats, sheep.</b> Three species, corresponding to <i>kohanim,</i> Levites and Israelites, and corresponding to the Torah, the Prophets, and the Sacred Scripture. Three fives, corresponding to the five <i>chumashim</i> [of the Torah], to the five commandments written on the one tablet, and five commandments written on the other. Until here, [my remarks are] from the commentary of R’ Moshe Hadarshan. 

Verse 24

<b>On the third day, the leader etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>On the third day, the leader who brought the offering was from the sons of Zevulun, and so with all of them. But with Nesanel, concerning whom it is said, “Nesanel brought forth,” the proper succeeding words are “leader of Yissachar,” since it has already mentioned his name and that he brought. With the others, about whom it does not say “he brought,” the proper words are these: “the leader of the children of so-and-so,” that day, the leader who brought was from the tribe of so-and-so.

Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28

Verse 71

Verse 73



Verse 74



Verse 75



Verse 76

Verse 79

Verse 81



Verse 82



Verse 83



Verse 84

<b>On the day it was anointed.</b> On the very day it was anointed, he (each leader) brought the offering. Then how do I justify “after it was anointed”? [To teach] That it was anointed first, and then he brought the offering. But, perhaps “after it was anointed” [means] after a time, and “on the day it was anointed” merely teaches that it was anointed by day? When it says “on the day they were anointed,” we learn that it was anointed by day. Then why does the Torah write “on the day it was anointed”? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>On the day it was anointed, he brought the offering. 
<b>Twelve silver trays.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>These were the very ones that were donated, none were disqualified. 

Verse 85

<b>One hundred thirty [shekolim was the weight of] each tray.</b> Why does the Torah say this? Because it said “one hundred thirty [<i>shekolim</i> was] its weight,” but does not explain <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>by which <i>shekel</i> standard. Therefore, Scripture repeats it here, and includes everything — “all the silver of the vessels” — in the <i>shekel</i> of the sacred standard. 
<b>All the silver vessels, etc.</b> This teaches you that the Sanctuary vessels were weighed with <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>precision. Whether weighed individually or collectively, there was neither excess nor shortfall. 

Verse 86

<b>Twelve golden spoons.</b> Why is this said? Because it says, “one spoon of ten gold,” [meaning] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>it was golden, and it weighed ten silver <i>shekolim</i>. But perhaps [it means] one silver spoon, weighing ten golden <i>shekolim</i> — and the golden <i>shekolim</i> are not the same weight as the silver ones? — The Torah therefore writes “golden spoons” — they (the spoons) were gold. 


Verse 87



Verse 88



Verse 89

<b>When Moshe would enter.</b> When two passages conflict, a third decides between them. One passage says: “God spoke to him from the Tent of Meeting” — this was outside the <i>paroches</i> partition. And one passage says: “I will speak to you from above the cover [of the Ark].” This [passage] comes and decides between them. Moshe came to the Tent of Meeting. There he heard the Voice coming from above the cover. <b>Between the two cherubs.</b> The Voice emanated from heaven to the space between the two cherubs, and from there to the Tent of Meeting. 

<b>He would hear the Voice.</b> Perhaps the Voice was low (of a lesser degree)? The Torah therefore writes אֶת הַקּוֹל, “the Voice” — the Voice spoken to him at Sinai. But when it reached the doorway, it ceased, and did not go out of the tent. 
<b>Being spoken.</b> As being spoken unto Itself. It is respectful to the One above to speak thusly. He was speaking to Himself, and Moshe was listening in. 
<b>He spoke to him.</b> This excludes Aharon from the communications. 


Chapter 8



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>When you light.</b> Why is the <i>parshah</i> of the Menorah adjacent to the <i>parshah</i> of the leaders? Because when Aharon saw the leaders’ dedication (offerings) he was humiliated, since he did not join them in the dedication, neither he nor his tribe. The Holy One, Blessed is He, said to him, “By your life, yours is greater than theirs! For you will light and cleanse the lamps.” 
<b>When you light (lit. cause to rise).</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because the flame rises, igniting is described in terms of “rising.” He is required to ignite [the lamp] until the flame rises by itself. In addition, the Rabbis derive from here <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that there was a platform before the Menorah, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>upon which the <i>kohein</i> stood when he lit [the lamps]. 
<b>Toward the face of the Menorah.</b> Toward the middle lamp which was not on one of the branches, but on the Menorah itself. 
<b>Shall the seven lamps cast [their] light.</b> The six [lamps] that were on the six branches [and one on its stem]. The three eastern ones turned toward the middle [by] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>their wicks. Similarly, the three western ones — the heads of their wicks [were] towards the middle. Why? So that it whould not be said that He (God) needs the light. 

Verse 3

<b>Aharon did so.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To indicate his [Aharon’s] virtue — he did not digress. 


Verse 4

<b>This is how the Menorah was made.</b> The Holy One, Blessed is He, showed him (Moshe) by pointing [as one would point] with the finger, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>since he had difficulty with it. This is why it says וְזֶה (“This”). 
<b>Beaten.</b> <i>Batedic</i> (hammered) in Old French, meaning the same as דָּא לְדָא נָקְשָׁן, (“they struck one another”). There was a <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>lump of gold, [weighing] a <i>kikar,</i> [which] he beat with a hammer and cut with <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>shears to extend its (the Menorah’s) limbs properly; but it was not made limb by limb and [then] connected. 
<b>From its base until its flowers.</b> Its base was the hollow box over the legs, hollowed like the silver candelabras before princes. 
<b>From its base until its flowers.</b> As if to say, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”The Menorah proper, in its entirety, and all its dependent parts.” 
<b>From its base.</b> Which was a large limb.
<b>Until its flowers.</b> Its most <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>delicate work — it was all one piece. עַד (“until”), is customarily used in this sense, like “From the harvested crop, until the standing grain, and until the olive grove.” 
<b>According to the vision which [Adonoy] showed . . . </b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>According to the form which He showed him on the mountain (Sinai), as it is said: “Observe and make them according to the form. . .etc.” 
<b>So he made the Menorah.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The one who made it. But Midrash Aggadah [states] by the Holy One, Blessed is He, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>it was made spontaneously. 

Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>Take the Levites.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Take them with words of persuasion, “you are fortunate to merit becoming servants of the Omnipresent.” 


Verse 7

<b>Sprinkle them with the sin-offering waters.</b> Of the ashes of the red cow, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for some of them were defiled by contact with the dead. 
<b>And cause a razor to pass.</b> I found in R’ Moshe Hadarshan’s remarks: “Because they were given in atonement for the firstborn <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>who practiced idolatry, which is referred to as ‘sacrificing to the dead,’ and since the leper is considered dead, they required shaving like lepers.” 

Verse 8

<b>They should take a young bullock.</b> This was a burnt-offering, as it is written, “he should make . . . one a burnt-offering.” This is the communal sacrifice for idolatry. 
<b>And a second bullock.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>What does the Torah teach [by specifying] ‘a second’? To inform you that, just as the burnt-offering was not eaten, so was the sin-offering not eaten. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This supports his remarks, from Toras Kohanim. Now I say <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that it was a temporary ruling, as they should have brought a goat as a sin-offering for idolatry with the burnt-offering bull. 

Verse 9

<b>And you shall gather the entire congregation</b> Since the Levites are given as an atonement-offering in their place, let them come <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and stand near their offering and rest their hands on them. 


Verse 10



Verse 11

<b>Aharon shall wave the Levites as a wave-offering</b> Just as the leper’s guilt- offering <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>requires waving when it is still alive. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Three wavings were stated in this chapter: The first, of the sons of Kehos. Therefore it is stated of them: “They will be [entrusted] to do the worship of Adonoy,” since the work of the holiest is upon them — the Ark and the Table etc. The second, of the sons of Gershon. It is therefore stated of them: “A wave-offering to Adonoy,” for even they were entrusted with holy work — tapestries and the hooks which were seen in the Holy of Holies. And the third, of the sons of Merori. 


Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>They are given; they are given.</b> Given for carrying, given for singing. 
<b> פִּטְרַת</b> The opening of.

Verse 17

<b>For every first born is Mine.</b> The first born were Mine by the rules of justice, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>since I protected them among the Egyptian firstborn. So I took them for Myself — until they strayed with the [golden] calf. Now I have taken the Levites. 


Verse 18



Verse 19

<b>I have given the Levites, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Bnei Yisroel are mentioned five times, in this passage, to make their preciousness known. They are remembered repeatedly in a single passage to correspond with the number of the five books of the Torah. I saw this in Bereishis Rabbah. 
<b>So that there will not be a plague among Bnei Yisroel.</b> So that they will not need <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to approach the Holy, for if they approach, there will be a plague. 

Verse 20

<b>Moshe, Aharon, and the entire congregation did, etc.</b> Moshe placed them, Aharon waved them, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the Israelites rested their hands. 

Verse 21



Verse 22

<b>Just as Adonoy commanded, etc. so they did.</b> This indicates the praiseworthiness of those who did, and those with whom it was done — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>no one objected. 


Verse 23



Verse 24

<b>This concerns the Levites.</b> Age disqualifies them, but physical deformity does not disqualify them. 
<b>From the age of twenty-five.</b> But elsewhere it says, “From the age of thirty.” How is this reconciled? From the age of twenty-five he begins to study of the laws of the service. He studies for five years, and serves at the age of thirty. From here [we derive] that a pupil who does not see <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>favorable indications in his studies for five years will never see (them). 

Verse 25

<b>And shall no longer work.</b> At the task of carrying <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>on the shoulder, but he returns to lock the gates, to sing, and to load the wagons. This is [the meaning of] “But he shall serve <i>his</i> brethren,” ‘<i>with</i> his brethren’, as Targum [Onkelos] renders. 

Verse 26

<b>To keep the watch.</b> To camp around the Tent, and erect and dismantle [it] during the journeys. 


Chapter 9



Verse 1

<b>In the first month.</b> The chapter at the beginning of this book <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>was not said until Iyar. You learn, that there is no order of precedence or succession in the Torah. But why did He not begin with this [chapter]? Because it is to Yisroel’s discredit, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that throughout the forty years that Yisroel was in the wilderness they offered no other <i>Pesach</i>-offering but this. 

Verse 2

<b>In its proper time.</b> Even on Shabbos; <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>even during ritual uncleanliness. 


Verse 3

<b>According to all its statutes.</b> These are the commandments pertaining to its body [i.e., the animal itself] a lamb; unblemished; male; a yearling. 
<b>And according to all its laws.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>These are commandments having a bearing on the animal but originate from another place (i.e., outside the animal) For example, the seven days of eating <i>matzoh</i> and of eliminating <i>chometz</i>. ([An alternate text:] The commandments pertaining to its body — a lamb; unblemished; male; a yearling. Having a bearing on the animal; roasted over fire, its head with its knees and its inner organs. Outside its body — <i>matzoh</i> and eliminating <i>chometz.</i>) 

Verse 4

<b>Moshe spoke, etc.</b> What does the Torah teach? Does it not say, “Moshe spoke <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>of God’s holidays”? Evidently, when he heard the <i>parshah</i> of the holidays at Sinai, he told it to them, and then he reviewed it and exhorted them at the time it was to be performed. 

Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>Before Moshe and before Aharon.</b> When both were seated in the study hall, they approached them and asked. But it is untenable to say [that they asked them] one after the other, for if Moshe did not know, how would Aharon [know]? 


Verse 7

<b>Why should we be excluded.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He (Moshe) said to them: “The sacred offerings cannot be brought during ritual impurity.” They said to him: “[But] let the blood be sprinkled on us by ritually pure <i>kohanim</i> and the flesh eaten by those who are pure.” He said to them: “Wait, while I listen,” like a disciple assured of hearing from his master’s mouth. Fortunate is the mortal thus assured, for whenever he wished, he could speak with the Divine Presence. Now <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>this chapter should appropriately have been said through Moshe, as is all the rest of the Torah. But these [people] gained the merit of having it said through them, because Providence brings about merit through the meritorious. 


Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10

<b>Or on a distant road.</b> There is a dot over this, as if to say: Not that it was definitely distant, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but that he was outside the threshold of the [Temple] courtyard thoughout the time for slaughtering [the Pesach]. [At] the second <i>Pesach, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>matzoh</i> and <i>chometz</i> may be with him at home; it is not considered ‘<i>yom tov</i>’; and <i>chometz</i> is not prohibited except while he eats [the <i>korbon</i>]. 


Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14

<b>If a proselyte dwells among you, and brings the Pesach-offering.</b> Perhaps everyone who converts must immediately bring the <i>Pesach</i>-offering? The Torah therefore teaches, “One statute, etc . . .” Rather, this is its meaning: “If a proselyte dwells among you, and he comes to bring the <i>Pesach</i>-offering with his fellows, according to the statutes of the <i>Pesach</i>-offering and its laws shall he do.” 


Verse 15

<b>The Mishkon [which served] as the Tent of Testimony.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The <i>Mishkon</i> which was made to be a tent for the tablets of testimony.
<b>There was over the <i>Mishkon.</i></b> Similar to, “would constantly be” over the <i>Mishkon.</i> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Similarly, all the usages in the <i>parshah.</i> 


Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>The Cloud was lifted.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, אִסְתַּלָּקוּת, (“was lifted”). Similarly, “the Cloud <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>was lifted.” But it would be improper to write “According to when the Cloud rose,” “the Cloud rose,” because the connotation is not rising, but flowering and ascending, as in, “behold, a tiny cloud, like a man’s palm, rises from the sea.” 

Verse 18

<b>On the word of Adonoy did they travel.</b> We learned in [the Beraysa describing] the work of the <i>Mishkon</i>; When the Israelites were departing the Cloud column would fold, and extend over the tribe of Yehudah like a type of beam. They sounded the <i>tekiah, teruah,</i> and <i>tekiah. But it did not proceed until Moshe intoned, “Rise, Adonoy . . .” Then the banner of the camp of Yehudah departed. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is in Sifri. </i>
<b>On the word of Adonoy did they camp.</b> When the Israelites were camping, the Cloud column would mushroom upward and extend over the tribe of Yehudah like a type of protective covering. It did not separate until Moshe said, “Come to rest, Adonoy, among the myriads and thousands of Israel.” Thus you say, “on the order of Adonoy, through Moshe.” 

Verse 19



Verse 20

<b>Sometimes (lit. there is).</b> As if to say, “sometimes.” 
<b>A number of days.</b> “a few days.” 


Verse 21



Verse 22

<b>Or a year. (lit. days).</b> A year, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as in “[יָמִים], a year shall be its redemption [period].” 

Chapter 10



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>(Make for yourself.</b> So that they they may sound the trumpet before you like a king, as it is said, “There was a king among the righteous.” 
<b>Make for yourself.</b> From your own resources.
<b>Make for yourself.</b> You shall make them and use them, but no one else.) 
<b>To summon the congregation.</b> When you want to speak with the Sanhedrin or the rest of the people, and you summon them to gather before you, summon them with the trumpets. 
<b>And to initiate the departure of the camps.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>At the time of the camps’ departure, sound them as a signal. Consequently, you say that they departed on the basis of three [initiatives]. By the word of the Holy One, Blessed is He; by the word of Moshe; and by the trumpets. 
<b>Beaten.</b> From a [single] ingot you should make it, by beating [it] with a hammer. 

Verse 3

<b>When they will blow them.</b> Both of them. This is the signal for summoning the community, as it is said, “The entire community shall present itself to you at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting.” 

Verse 4
