<b>Cattle and sheep.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>A small amount — only one of the cattle, and one sheep. 


Verse 41

<b>Bamos Ba’al.</b> As Targum [Onklos] renders, “To the heights of his deity.” [Ba’al is] the name of an idol. 

Chapter 23



Verse 1



Verse 2



Verse 3

<b>Perhaps, Adonoy will appear to me.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He does not usually speak with me by day. 
<b>He went away alone.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] translates, “alone.” The word denotes placidity and quiet, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as nothing but silence accompanied him. 

Verse 4

<b>Chanced to appear.</b> The word denotes a casual occurrence; it denotes disgrace; <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>it denotes the uncleanness of seminal emission. As if to say, “reluctantly and in humiliation.” He appeared to him by day only in order to display the preciousness of Bnei Yisroel.’ 
<b>The seven altars.</b> “I have arranged seven altars” is not written here, but אֶת־שִׁבְעַת הַמִּזְבְּחֹת . He (Bil’am) said before Him: “Their patriarchs built seven altars before you, so I arranged [altars] to correspond with all of them. Avrohom built four: “He built an altar there to God, who had appeared to him.” “From there, he moved to the mountain, etc.,” “Avraham pitched his tent, etc.,” and one on Mount Moriah. Yitzchak built one: “He built an altar there, etc.” Ya’akov built two: One in Shechem, and one in Beis El. 
<b>And I offered an ox and a ram on the altar.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But Avraham only offered up a single ram. 


Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7

<b>Curse Yaakov for me; Go, invoke wrath against Yisroel.</b> He instructed him to curse them <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>with both names, in case one of them was not the principal one. 

Verse 8

<b>How can I curse, when God has not cursed.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When they deserved to have been cursed, they were not cursed. When their father mentioned their sin, “For they killed a man in their rage,” he cursed only their rage, as it is said, “Cursed is their rage.” When their father entered deceitfully to his father, he deserved to have been cursed. What is said there? “Let him also be blessed.” Of those who were to declare blessings it is said, “these [tribes] shall stand to bless the people.” Of those who were to declare curses, is not said, “these shall stand to curse the people,” but “these shall stand at the curse” — He did not want to invoke the word “curse” against them. 
<b>If Adonoy has not been angry.</b> I have no power, except that I know how to pinpoint the moment when the Holy One, Blessed is He, is angry. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But He was not angry during all those days that I came to you. This is why it is said, “My people, remember, now, what [Balak] advised, etc., and what Bil’am replied to him, etc., so that you may know God’s righteousness.” 

Verse 9

<b>For I view it from the mountain peaks (lit. head of the mountains).</b> I gaze at their origins, the beginnings of their roots, and I perceive that they are well founded <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and powerful, like the mountains and the hills, because of the patriarchs and the matriarchs. 
<b>Behold! A people which shall dwell alone.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This was acquired for them by their forefathers — to dwell alone, as rendered by Targum [Onkelos]. 
<b>And will not be reckoned among the nations.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] explains, they will not be annihilated with the other nations, as it is said, “for I shall annihilate all the nations, etc.” They will not be reckoned with the rest. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: When they rejoice, no nation rejoices with them, as it is said, “God shall give them repose alone.” But when the nations prosper, they partake with each of them, without debiting the balance of their account. This is [the meaning of] “and will not be reckoned among the nations.” 

Verse 10

<b>Who can count the dust of Yaakov.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As Targum [Onkelos] interprets, “the children of the house of Yaakov, etc., . . . of the four camps” — of the four banners. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation [of] the dust of Yaakov, One cannot reckon the commandments which they perform with dust. “Do not plow with an ox and a donkey,” “do not plant <i>kilayim,</i>” the dust of the [red] cow, the dust of the <i>sotah,</i> and similar ones. 
<b>Or count the seed of Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The seed which emanates during their intercourse.
<b>May my soul die the death of the righteous.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Among them.

Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13

<b>Curse them for me.</b> The word denotes a command: “Curse them for me.”

Verse 14

<b>Field of Tzofim.</b> This was an elevated area where a lookout was stationed to watch for forces which might approach the city.
<b>To the peak of the mountain.</b> Bil’am was not as great a sorcerer as Balak. Balak divined that Bnei Yisroel would suffer a severe breach there, for Moshe died there. He thought that the curse would descend upon them from there, that this is the breach that I divine. 


Verse 15

<b>I will be called here by chance.</b> By the Holy One, blessed is He. <b>I will be called by chance.</b> This denotes the reflexive usage.

Verse 16

<b>And placed the word in his mouth.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>What is this placing, and what would Scripture have been lacking if it had said, “return to Balak and say the following”? But when he heard that he was not permitted to curse, he said, “Why should I return to Balak merely to bring him grief”? So the Holy One, Blessed is He, placed a rein and a bit in his mouth, like a man who equips his animal with a bit to lead it wherever he wishes. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He said to him, “You will be forced to return to Balak.” 


Verse 17

<b>Accompanied by the Moavite dignitaries.</b> Above it states “and <i>all</i> the Moavite dignitaries.” When they saw that it was hopeless, some departed, leaving only some others. 
<b>What did Adonoy say?</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This denotes derision, as if to say, “you are not your own master.” 

Verse 18

<b>Arise, Balak.</b> When he saw that he was ridiculing him, he intended to irritate him. “Stand on your feet! You are not permitted to remain seated while I serve as the Omnipresent’s emissary to you.” 
<b>Son of (lit. his son) Tzipor.</b> This is a Scriptural usage, like “beasts (lit. his beasts) of the forest,” “beasts (lit. his beasts) of the earth,” “into a spring (lit. his spring) of water.” 

Verse 19

<b>God is not like man, etc.</b> He has already sworn to them to bring them and give them possession of the land of the seven nations, and you think that you can kill them in the wilderness? 
<b>Would He say, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The word denotes a question. Targum [Onkelos] translates “who retract and reconsider” — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they retract, then reconsider whether to change their minds. 

Verse 20

<b>Behold I was commanded to bless.</b> You ask me, “what has God said”? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I have received [instructions] from Him to bless them. <b>[Bless.</b> Similar “to bless.”]
<b>[When] He has blessed, I cannot reverse it.</b> He has blessed them, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and I will not reverse his blessing. 
<b>He has blessed.</b> As if it were וּבִרֵךְ . This is how the letter ר is conjugated, like אוֹיֵב חֵרֵף, as if it were חִרֵף . Similarly, וּבֹצֵעַ בֵּרֵךְ One who lauds and blesses the thief, saying “have no fear, you will not be punished, you will be at peace,” angers the Holy One, Blessed is He. But one cannot say that בֵּרֵךְ is a noun, for if so, it would be vocalized with a minor <i>patach</i> [<i>segol,</i> בֶּרֶךְ], with the accent above. However, because it connotes action, it is vocalized with a minor <i>komatz</i> [<i>tzayreh,</i> בֵּרֵךְ], with the accent below. 

Verse 21

<b>One does not see evildoers in Yaakov.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders. Another interpretation: By following its plain meaning, it may be expounded beautifully. The Holy One, Blessed is He, does not look at the evil in Yaakov. When they transgress His commandments, He does not pursue them exactingly by reflecting on <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the wickedness and wrongdoing of their violation of His doctrines. 

<b>Transgression.</b> The word [עמל, (lit. tediousness)] denotes sin, as in “sin conceives,” “for you observe sinful and infuriating behaviour.” Because sinfulness is tedious before the Omnipresent. 
<b>Adonoy, his God, is with him.</b> Even when they anger Him and are rebellious, He does not leave them. 
<b>He has the King’s friendship.</b> The word denotes affection and friendship, like “David’s comrade” — one who loves David, “and he gave it to his fellow.” Similarly, Onkelos renders “the King’s Presence is among them.” 

Verse 22

<b>God Who has brought them out of Egypt.</b> You said, “behold, a nation came out of Egypt” — they did not leave by themselves, God delivered them. 
<b>Has shown His great strength to them.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like the power of His loftiness and elevation. Similarly, “and silver [shall be your] strength.” It denotes strength. Now I say that the word [תּוֹעֲפֹת] is from וְעוֹף יְעוֹפֵף. (“and let birds fly,”) someone who flies to a lofty elevation — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>this is a great application of power. וְתוֹעֲפֹת רְאֵם, lofty flight. Another interpretation [of] תוֹעֲפֹת רְאֵם, “the power of the <i>re’emim.</i>” The Rabbis explain that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>this refers to the demons and evil spirits. 

Verse 23

<b>For there is no sorcery in Yaakov.</b> For they deserve to be blessed, since there are no sorcerers or magicians among them. 

<b>In due time, it will be said to Yaakov, etc.</b> There is destined <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to be another time such as this, when their preciousness will be revealed before everyone’s eyes, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for they will be seated before Him studying the Torah from His mouth, and their partition will be further within, than the administering angels, who will ask them, “What has God done”? This is [the meaning of] what is said, “your eyes shall behold your master.” Another interpretation: יֵאָמֵר לְיַעֲקֹב does not refer to the future, but to the present. They have no need for magicians and sorcerers, for at any time when it is necessary that Yaakov and Yisroel be told what the Holy One, Blessed is He, has done, and what He has decreed on high, they do not perform magic or sorcery. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Rather, they are told through their prophets what the Omnipresent’s decree is, or, the <i>Urim</i> and <i>Tummim</i> informs them. Onkelos, however, does not interpret this way. 


Verse 24

<b>Behold, a people that rises like a young lion, etc.</b> When they rise from their slumber in the morning, they are as vigorous as the young lion and the lion, to snatch the <i>mitzvos</i> wearing a <i>Tallis,</i> reading the <i>Shema,</i> and putting on the <i>Tefillin.</i> 
<b>He does not lie down.</b> At night on his bed <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>until he consumes and destroys every harmful spirit which comes to attack him. How is this? He reads the bedtime <i>Shema,</i> and entrusts his soul in the hand of the Omnipresent. If a corps or army comes to attack them, the Holy One, Blessed is He, protects them — and fights their battles, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>strikes them (the attackers) dead. Another interpretation of “behold, a people rises like a lion, etc.,” is as Targum [Onkelos] renders. 
<b>And drinks the blood of its kill.</b> He prophesied that Moshe would not die <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>until he would strike the Midianite kings dead, and he (Bil’am) would be killed with them, as it is said, “and Bil’am the son of Beor, the sorcerer, the Bnei Yisroel killed by the sword, with the others whom they killed.” 

Verse 25

<b>Also do not curse them.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The first “also” is added to the second “also,” and the second “also” to the first “also.” Similarly, “also to me, also to you, let him not be.” Similarly, “also the youth, also the virgin.” 


Verse 26



Verse 27

<b>And you will curse them for me.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is not a command, like “curse them,” but the future tense. “Perhaps it will be proper in His eyes, and you will curse them for me, from there.” “<i>Malduras lui</i>” (you will curse them), in Old French. 

Verse 28

<b>To the peak of Pe’or.</b> Balak was a great sorcerer, and he saw that they were destined to be smitten through Pe’or, but he didn’t know in what way. He said, “Perhaps the curse will descend on them from there.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>It is similar with all the star gazers — they see, but do not know what they see. 


Chapter 24



Verse 1

<b>Bil’am saw that it was favorable, etc.</b> He said, “it is no longer necessary for me to test the Holy One, Blessed is He, for He will never want to curse them. 
<b>He did not approach, as at each time.</b> As he had done twice. 
<b>Towards sorcery.</b> To divine whether God would perhaps chance to appear to him as he wished. He said, “Whether or not He wants to curse them, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I will mention their sins, so that the curse will descend with the mention of their sins.” 
<b>He set his face toward the wilderness.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As Targum [Onkelos] renders. 


Verse 2

<b>Bil’am raised his eyes.</b> He strove <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to induce the evil eye in them. Here you have his three characteristics, the evil eye, false vanity, and greed, as stated above. 
<b>Encamped according to its tribes.</b> He saw each tribe dwelling by itself, without mingling. He saw that their entrances did not face each other, so that one should not look into his neighbor’s tent. 
<b>And the spirit of God rested upon him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>It occurred to him not to curse them. 


Verse 3

<b>The son of (lit. his son was) Be’or.</b> Like לְמַעְיְנוֹ מָיִם, “into a spring of water.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>According to Midrash Aggadah: Both were greater than their forefathers; “Balak, his son Tzipor” — his father was his son in royalty, and Bil’am was greater than his father in prophecy, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he was a coin, the son of half a coin. 
<b>Of the open-socketed eye.</b> His eye had been put out and removed, and its socket appeared open. The word [שְׁתֻם] is in the Mishnah; <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”enough for it to have been opened, sealed, and dried.” The Rabbis remark, because he said, “He counts the seed of Yisroel” — that the Holy One, Blessed is He, sits and counts the seed of the Israelites, awaiting the drop from which a saint will be born, he thought, “the One who is Holy, and whose ministering angels are holy, looks at these things”? For this, Bil’am’s eye was blinded. However, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>some interpret שְׁתֻם הָעָיִן as “of the open eye,” as Targum [Onkelos] renders. And since he said “of the open eye,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but did not say “of the open eyes,” we learn that he was blind in one of his eyes. 

Verse 4

<b>Fallen, with opened eyes.</b> The plain interpretation is like Targum [Onkelos], that He (God) did not reveal Himself to him except at night, when he was lying down. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>According to Midrash, when He revealed Himself to him, he did not have the strength to stand on his feet, but fell to his face, because he was uncircumcised, and it was disgusting to be revealed to him when he stood upright before Him. 

Verse 5

<b>How goodly are your tents.</b> Because he saw that their entrances were not facing each other.
<b>Your dwelling places.</b> Your camps, as Targum [Onkelos] renders. Another interpretation of how goodly are your tents: How goodly is the tent of Shiloh and the Eternal Temple when they are inhabited, for sacrifices are offered in them to bring you forgiveness. 
<b>Your dwelling places.</b> Even when they are desolate, since they are held as security for you, and their desolation brings atonement for your souls, as it is said, “Adonoy expended his fury” — and how did He expend it? “He ignited a fire in Tziyon.” 

Verse 6

<b>They stretch forth like streams.</b> Which extend and flow, stretching across the distance. The Rabbis remark, ‘from that wicked one’s blessings, we learn how he intended to curse them, when he decided to set his face towards the wilderness. When the Omnipresent overturned [the words of] his mouth, his blessings corresponded with his intended curses, etc.,’ as stated in “Chelek.” 
<b>Like the aloe trees.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, meaning the same as “myrrh and aloes.” 
<b>That Adonoy has planted.</b> In the garden of Eden. Another interpretation of כַּאֲהָלִים נָטַע ה', like the heavens stretched taut like a tent [as it is said, “He stretched them taut like a tent to be dwelt in”]. 
<b>That Adonoy has planted,</b> The expression נְטִיעָה is found with relation to tents, as it is said, “he stretched taut his palatial tents.” 


Verse 7

<b>From his buckets.</b> From his wells. The explanation is as Targum [Onkelos] interprets.
<b>And his seed will have an abundant flow.</b> This denotes success, like a seed planted near water. 
<b>His king will be greater than Agag.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Their first king shall conquer Agag, king of Amalek. 
<b>And his monarchy shall be uplifted.</b> Yaakov’s [monarchy] more and more, as he (Shaul) shall be followed by Dovid and Shlomo. 

Verse 8

<b>God Who has brought him out of Egypt.</b> Who gave them this eminence? God, who delivered them from Egypt <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>with his power and exaltedness, shall consume the nations who oppress him. 
<b>Their bones.</b> Of the oppressors.
<b>He shall crush.</b> Menachem interprets this as denoting breaking. Similarly, “[wolves in the evening] who did not break any bones in the morning.” Similarly, “you shall crush its earthen vessels.” I say that the meaning is “bone.” He strips the surrounding flesh with his teeth, and the marrow from inside, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>leaving the bone exposed. 
<b>And dip His arrows [in their blood].</b> Onkelos interprets “the oppressors’ half,” their portion, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>like בַּעֲלֵי חִצִּים, [translated as] מָרֵי פַלְגּוּתָא (meaning portion, or half), יִמְחָץ is similar, meaning the same as “she split [his skull], passing through his forehead” — they shall apportion their land. Also, this may be interpreted as actually denoting arrows. The arrows of the Holy One, Blessed is He, will יִמְחַץ in the blood of the oppressors, He shall dip and stain with their blood, as in, “that your foot may wade through blood” This is not a departure from the connotation of “wound,” as in “I have wounded,” since someone stained with blood appears to have been injured and wounded. 


Verse 9

<b>He crouches and lies like a lion.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, they will settle in their land with strength and power. 

Verse 10

<b>[He] clapped his hands.</b> He struck one against the other.

Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13

<b>Transgress the word of Adonoy.</b> Here “<i>my</i>” God is not stated, as it was originally, for he knew that he was loathed by the Holy One, Blessed is He, and that he had been repudiated. 


Verse 14

<b>Am returning to my people.</b> I am now like the rest of my people — the Holy One, Blessed is He, had forsaken him. 
<b>Come, I will advise you.</b> Concerning the action you should take. What was the advice? The God of these people hates promiscuity, etc., as stated in “Chelek.” The proof that Bil’am instigated his advice so that they would be ensnared into immorality is from Scripture’s declaration, “they were involved with the Israelites through Bil’am’s advice.” 
<b>What this people will do to your people.</b> This is a shortened passage; I will advise you about ensnaring them, and I will tell you how they are destined to destroy Moav at the end of days — “and smash the great men of Moav.” Targum [Onkelos] explains where the Hebrew falls short. 

Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>And knows the thoughts of the Most Exalted.</b> To pinpoint the moment of His anger.

Verse 17

<b>I see it.</b> I see the praise and greatness of Yaakov. Not, however, now, but at a later time. 
<b>A star has gone forth.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] interprets. דָּרַךְ means the same as דָּרַךְ קַשְׁתּוֹ, “He hurled with His bow,” as a star travels like an arrow. In Old French, “<i>destente</i>” (“hurl”). As if to say, “a constellation shall rise.” 
<b>A staff has arisen.</b> A king who subdues and rules.
<b>Smash the corners of Moav.</b> This refers to David, of whom it is said, “he laid them on the ground and measured two strings to kill, etc.” 
<b>And impale.</b> The meaning is to penetrate, like, “I have excavated,” “the pit ax which quarried you” “let the ravens of the river gouge it.” “<i>Forjier</i>” (“pierce”), in Old French. 
<b>All of the sons of Sheis.</b> All the nations, since they were all descended from Sheis, the son of Adam. 

Verse 18

<b>Seir shall become the possession of his enemies.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>His enemies, the Bnei Yisroel. 

Verse 19

<b>A ruler shall come from Yaakov.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Yet another ruler shall come from Yaakov.
<b>Who will annihilate the survivors of the city.</b> Of the most prominent city of Edom, Rome. He said this concerning King Mashiach, of whom it is said, “he shall rule from sea to sea,” “there will be no survivors of the house of Eisav.” 

Verse 20

<b>[Bil’am] Saw Amalek.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He gazed at Amalek’s punishment.
<b>Amalek was the first among nations.</b> He preceded them all <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in waging war against Israel. This, too, is Targum’s [Onkelos] interpretation. <b>And his end.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Will be to perish by their hand, as it is said, “you shall obliterate the memory of Amalek.” 

Verse 21

<b>He saw the Keinite.</b> Because the Keinite was encamped near Amalek, as in the incident of which it is said, “Shaul said to the Keinite, etc.,” he mentioned him after Amalek. He gazed at the greatness of Yisro’s descendants, of whom it is said, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”Tirasites, Shimasites, Sochasites.” 
<b>How powerful is your dwelling place.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I wonder how you merited this. Were you not with me in counseling “come, let us deal shrewdly with them”? Yet now you have settled yourself in the power and strength of Israel. 

Verse 22

<b>For, if Kayin is to be uprooted, etc.</b> How fortunate you are to be encamped in this stronghold, so that you will no longer be driven from the world. For, even if you are destined to be exiled with the ten tribes, and will be uprooted from the place where you settled, what of it? 
<b>Until where (lit. what) will Ashur take you captive.</b> Until where will he exile you? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Perhaps to Chalach and Chavor? This is not considered being driven from the world, but being shifted from place to place, and you shall return with the other exiles. 

Verse 23

<b>He set forth his parable, etc.</b> Since he mentioned the captivity by Ashur, he said: Alas! who can survive from God’s devastation <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Who is capable of self-survival against His putting these — so that He shall not put them [into effect] against him — He who decrees (God) — these? Sancheriv shall arise and commingle all the nations. Furthermore, Warships will come from Kittim — Kitites, meaning Romans, shall go forth in great ships against Ashur. 

Verse 24


<b>And cause suffering to those at the other side.</b> Shall cause suffering for those at the other side of the river.
<b>They, too, shall be lost for eternity.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Similarly, Doniel explains, “until the animal was killed, and its body destroyed.” 
<b>Warships.</b> Great ships, as it is written, וְצִי אַדִּיר, rendered by Targum as “great ships.” 

Chapter 25



Verse 1

<b>In Shittim.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This was its name. 

<b>Acting promiscuously with the daughters of Moav.</b> As a result of Bil’am’s advice, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as stated in “Chelek.” 

Verse 2

<b>And prostrated themselves before their gods.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When he was overcome by lust, and asked her to submit to him, she drew a statue of Pe’or from her bosom toward him and said, ‘Prostrate yourself before this’! 

Verse 3

<b>Pe’or.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because they bared, their buttocks before it and relieved themselves — this is the way it was worshipped. 

<b>The rage of Adonoy flared against Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He sent a plague on them.

Verse 4

<b>Take all the leaders of the people.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To pass judgement on those who worshipped Pe’or.
<b>And hang them.</b> The worshippers.
<b> וְהוֹקַע .</b> This refers to hanging, as we find concerning the sons of Shaul, “and let us hang them for [the sake of] God.” and there, hanging is specified, idolatry is [punished] with stoning, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>all those stoned are hung. 
<b>Facing the sun.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>In full public view. Midrash Aggadah: The sun identifies the sinners. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The cloud rolls back from the area above him, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and the sun shines on him. 

Verse 5

<b>Each of you must execute his men.</b> Each of the Israelite judges executed two men, and there were eighty eight thousand Israelite judges, as stated in Sanhedrin. 

Verse 6

<b>Behold, a man came from among Bnei Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The tribe of Shimon gathered around Zimri, who was their leader, and said to him, “We are being sentenced to death, and you sit by, etc.,” as stated in “Eilu Hein Hanisrafin.” 
<b>The Midianite woman.</b> Kozbi, daughter of Tzur. 
<b>Before the eyes of Moshe.</b> They said to him, “Moshe, is she forbidden or permitted? If you say ‘forbidden,’ <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>who permitted the daughter of Yisro to you? etc.” as stated there. 
<b>Who were weeping.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The <i>halachah</i> was concealed from him [that anyone having relations with a gentile woman is to be executed by the zealous], so they all burst into tears. At the golden calf, Moshe stood against six hundred thousand, as it is said, “he ground it into powder, etc.,” yet here he was enfeebled? But this was in order that Pinchas might come and take what was appropriately his. 

Verse 7

<b>Pinchas. . .saw.</b> He saw the incident <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and remembered the <i>halachah.</i> He said to Moshe, “I received from you [the teaching] that anyone having relations with a gentile woman is to be <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>executed by the zealous.” He replied to him, “Let the one who reads the correspondence serve as its executor.” Instantly, “he took a spear in his hand, etc.” 

Verse 8

<b> אֶל הַקֻבָּה .</b> Into the tent.
<b>Through her belly.</b> As in “the jaws and the uterus.” He struck precisely at Zimri’s male organ and her female organ, so everyone saw that he did not kill them needlessly. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Many miracles were performed for him, etc., as stated there. 


Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11

Pinchas the son of Elozor, the son of Aharon the kohein. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because the tri es disparaged him, [saying] ‘Have you seen that son of “Puti,” whose mother’s father fattened calves for idol worship, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>who murdered the chieftain of a tribe of Israel?’ Therefore, Scripture traces his lineage to Aharon. 

<b>By his vengeance for Me.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>By avenging My vengeance — by his rage where I should have been enraged. קִנְאָה always denotes someone <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>enflamed to avenge something. <i>Enportment,</i> “flaming anger,” in Old French. 

Verse 12

<b>My covenant [of] peace.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To be a covenant of peace for him like a man who harbors <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>gratitude and favor towards someone who benefitted him. Here, too, the Holy One, Blessed is He, expressed to him His peace. 


Verse 13

<b>It shall be.</b> To him — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>this covenant of Mine.
<b>A covenant of eternal kehunah.</b> Although the <i>kehunah</i> had already been given to Aharon’s descendants, it was given <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>solely to Aharon and his sons who were annointed with him, and to their generations who would be borne after their annointment. Pinchas, however, who was born before, and was not annointed, was not included in the <i>kehunah</i> until here. Similarly, we learned in Zevachim, ‘Pinchas was not rendered a <i>kohein until he killed Zimri.’ </i>
<b>For his God.</b> For the sake of his God, like הַמְקַנֵּא אַתָּה לִי, “are you zealous ‘for’ me?” and קִנֵּאתִי לְצִיּוֹן, “for the sake of Tzion.” 


Verse 14

<b>The name of the Israelite man, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Where he mentions the relationship of the saint for praise he mentions the relationship of the wicked for shame. 
<b>Leader of a paternal house of Shimon.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Of one of the five paternal houses of the tribe of Shimon. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: To proclaim the merit of Pinchas. Although this one was a leader, he did not refrain from avenging the desecration of the Name [of God]. This is why Scripture informs you of the identity of the one who was killed. 


Verse 15

<b>The name of the slain woman, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To inform you of the hatred of the Midianites, who abandoned a princess to promiscuous behavior in order to entice the Israelites into sinning. 

<b>The national leader.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>One of the five kings of Midian, “Evi, Rekem, Tzur, etc.” He was the most prominent of all of them, as it is said, “the national leader,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but because he debased himself by abandoning his daughter, he is counted third. 
<b>Of a paternal house.</b> There were five paternal houses in Midian, Eiphah, Eipher, Chanoch, Avidah, and Eldoah. This one was the king of one them. 

Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>Antagonize.</b> Like זָכוֹר, “remember,” שָׁמוֹר,”keep,” meaning ongoing action. It is incumbent upon you to act with hostility toward them. 

Verse 18

<b>For they antagonized you, etc., in the matter of Pe’or.</b> Since they abandoned their daughters to promiscuity <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in order to cause you to stray after Pe’or. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>However, He did not order the destruction of Moav, Because of Rus [Ruth], who was destined to emanate from them, as we state in Bava Kama. 


Chapter 26



Verse 1

<b>It was after the plague, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is compared to a shepherd whose flock was infiltrated by wolves, who killed some of them. He counted them, to ascertain the number of those remaining. Another interpretation: When they left Egypt and were entrusted to Moshe, they were given to him with a reckoning; now that he neared death, and the return of his sheep, he returned them with a reckoning. 


Verse 2

<b>According to their paternal house.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Their relationship follows the paternal tribe, rather than the maternal. 

Verse 3

<b>Moshe and Elozor the kohein spoke with them.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They spoke with them concerning this — that the Omnipresent had commanded to count them.
<b>Saying.</b> They said to them, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”You must be counted.” 

Verse 4

<b>[Count those] twenty years of age and above, as [Adonoy] commanded, etc.</b> That they be counted from the age of twenty and above, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as it is said, “everyone passing by to be counted, etc.” 


Verse 5

<b>The Chanochite family.</b> Because the gentiles disparaged them, saying, ‘what, they trace their lineage to their tribes? They think that the Egyptians had no control over their mothers? If they ruled over their bodies, then certainly over their wives!’ Therefore, the Holy One, Blessed is He, attached His Name to them, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the ה' on one side, and the י' on the other, to say, ‘I bear witness, concerning them, that they are the sons of their fathers.’ This is stated clearly by Dovid, “the tribes of God as a testimony to Israel.” This Name testifies for them concerning their tribes. Therefore, Scripture states, with all of them, הַחֲנוֹכִי, “the Chanochite,” הַפַּלּוּאִי, “the Paluite.” But with יִמְנָה, it was unnecessary to say מִשְׁפַּחַת הַיִּמְנִי, “the Yimnite family,” since the Name is fixed in it, the י' at the beginning and the ה' at the end. 

Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9

<b>Who incited</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Israel against Moshe.
<b>When they incited.</b> The people against God.
<b>Incited.</b> They misled the Israelites into quarreling with Moshe. This is the causative form.

Verse 10

<b>They became a symbol.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>A symbol and a reminder, so that no outsider would ever again come forward to dispute the <i>kehunah</i>. 

Verse 11

<b>But the sons of Korach did not die.</b> They were involved in the conspiracy at first, but during the dispute, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they repented in their hearts. Therefore, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>an elevated area was secured for them in <i>gehinom,</i> where they remained. 

Verse 12



Verse 13

<b>From Zerach.</b> This was Tzochar, meaning the same as “Tzohar,” illumination. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>However, the family of Ohad became extinct. Also, five [families] of the tribe of Binyamin, as he had descended to Egypt with ten sons, yet here only five are counted. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Also, Etzbon, of Gad — so there are seven families. I found, in the Talmud Yerushalmi, that when Aharon died the clouds of glory departed, and the Canaanites came to wage war against Israel. They (Bnei Yisroel) resolved to return to Egypt, and went back eight journeys, from Mount Hor to Moserah, as it is said, “Bnei Yisroel journeyed from Be’eros Bnei Yaakon to Moserah, where Aharon died.” Now did he not die at Mount Hor? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>And from Moserah to Mount Hor there are eight journeys going back. But, they returned, and the Levites pursued them to bring them back, killing seven of their families. And four Levite families fell; The families of Shim’i and Uzieli. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Of the sons of Yitzhar, none are counted here, except for the Korachite family. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I do not know the identity of the fourth. R’ Tanchuma expounded, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that they died in the plague at the affair of Bil’am — however, according to the loss suffered by the tribe of Shimon in this counting, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as compared with the first counting at the Sinai desert, it appears that all twenty four thousand <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>fell from the tribe of Shimon. 


Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>From Ozni.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I say that this was the family of Etzbon, but I do not know why his family was not called by his name. 


Verse 17



Verse 18



Verse 19



Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24

<b>From Yashuv.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is Yov, mentioned among those who went down to Egypt, as all of the families were called by the names of those who went down to Egypt. As for those who were born afterward, none of the families were called by their names, except for the families of Efrayim and Menashe, all of whom were born in Egypt, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and Ard and Na’aman, the sons of Bela, the son of Binyamin. I found, in the commentary of R’ Moshe Hadarshan, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that their mother went down to Egypt when she was pregnant with them, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they were, therefore, divided into separate families, like Chetzron and Chamul, who were Yehudah’s grandsons, and Chever and Malkiel, who were Asher’s grandsons. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>If this is from the Aggadah, fine, but if not, then I say that Bela had a great many grandchildren, and from those two, Ard and Na’aman, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>respectively, large families emanated. The descendants of the other children were called by Bela’s name, while the descendants of those two were called by their names. I say the same about the sons of Machir, who were divided into two families, one called by his name, and one called by the name of his son, Gil’ad. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Five families are missing from the sons of Binyamin. Here, his mother’s prophecy was partially fulfilled — she called him בֶּן אוֹנִי, “son of my sorrow.” With the concubine of Givah, it was completely fulfilled. I found this in the commentary of R’ Moshe Hadarshan. 


Verse 25



Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32



Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36

<b>These are the sons of Shuselach, etc.</b> The descendants of <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the other sons of Shuselach were called by the name Shuselach, but from Eiran a large family emanated, so it was called by his name. Thus, the sons of Shuselach were considered two families. Go and calculate, and you will discover, in this chapter, fifty seven families, and eight from the sons of Levi — hence, sixty five. This is [the meaning of] what is said, כִּי אַתֶּם "הַמְעַט" וְגוֹ', “for you are the least, etc. “ הֵ"א מְעַט, “five less.” You are five less than all the gentile families, as they are seventy. This, too, I understood from the commentary of R’ Moshe Hadarshan, but I had to subtract and add to his words. 


Verse 37



Verse 38

<b>From Achiram.</b> This is Eichi, who went down to Egypt. Because he was named to commemorate Yoseif, who was his brother and was exalted over him, he was called Achiram. 

Verse 39

<b>From Shfufam.</b> This is Mupim, to commemorate Yosef’s <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>being humbled among the nations. 


Verse 40



Verse 41



Verse 42

<b>From Shucham.</b> This is Chushim.

Verse 43



Verse 44



Verse 45



Verse 46

<b>The name of Asher’s daughter was Serach.</b> Because she remained alive, he counted her here. 


Verse 47



Verse 48



Verse 49



Verse 50



Verse 51



Verse 52



Verse 53

<b>The land shall be apportioned among these.</b> But not among those below the age of twenty, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>even if they reach twenty before the apportioning of the land. Indeed, the conquest lasted seven years, and the apportioning seven, yet no one received a portion in the land except for these six hundred and one thousand. If one of them had six sons, they received nothing but their father’s portion. 

Verse 54

<b>To the large [tribe], increase their inheritance.</b> To the tribe with the greater populace, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they gave a larger portion. Although the portions were unequal, as everything was assigned according to the size of the tribe, they implemented the apportioning solely by lots, and the lottery was inspired by the Sacred Spirit, as stated explicitly in Bava Basra. Elozor the <i>kohein</i> was clothed in the <i>Urim veTumim,</i> and said, with the Sacred Spirit, “If tribe so-and-so is drawn, then border so-and-so will be drawn with it.” The [names of the] tribes were written on twelve notes, and the twelve boundaries on twelve notes. They were mixed into a container, and the leader placed his hand into it and removed two notes. There appeared, in his hand, the note with the name of his tribe, and the note with the boundary specified for it. The lot itself would cry out, exclaiming, “I am the lot drawn for the so-and-so boundary, belonging to tribe so-and-so,” as it is said, “by word of the lottery.” The land was not apportioned dimensionally, since some boundaries were superior to others, but by assessed value. A poor <i>Kor</i> area was equivalent to a superior <i>Seah</i> area, all according to the value [of the soil.] 


Verse 55

<b>According to the names of their fathers’ tribes.</b> This refers to those who left Egypt. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Scripture deviates, with this inheritance, from all the others in the Torah. With every inheritance, the living inherit the dead, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but here, the dead inherit the living. How is this? Two brothers among those who left Egypt <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>had sons who entered the land, one had one son, the other, three. The single son received one portion, the three, three portions, as it is said, “the land shall be apportioned to these.” Their inheritance reverted <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to their grandfather, and they then shared everything equally. This is [the meaning of] what is said, “according to the names of their fathers’ tribes, they shall inherit” — after the sons received it, they reapportioned it according to the fathers who left Egypt. But if they had apportioned it originally among those numbered in the exodus from Egypt, the four would have received only two portions, whereas they now received four portions. 
<b>Only by lot.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This excludes Yehoshua and Kalev. And similarly it says, “they presented Kalev with Chevron, as Moshe had said.” And it says, “by the word of God they gave him the city which he requested.” 
<b>Of their fathers’ tribes.</b> This excludes proselytes and [gentile] slaves.

Verse 56

<b>By word of the lottery.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The lots spoke, as I explained above. This informs us that it was apportioned by the inspiration of the Sacred Spirit. This is why it is said, “By the word of God.” 

Verse 57



Verse 58

<b>These are the families of Levi.</b> There are missing, here, the families of Shim’i and Ozieili, and part of Yitzhari. 


Verse 59

<b>Whom [her mother] bore to Levi in Egypt.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Her birth was in Egypt, but she was not conceived in Egypt. As they were entering the wall, she bore her, and she completed the total of seventy. For, in enumeration, you will only find sixty-nine. 


Verse 60



Verse 61



Verse 62

<b>They were not counted among Bnei Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To have been counted from the age of twenty. What’s the reason? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Since no inheritance was given to them. Whereas those who were counted from the age of twenty were qualified to receive the inheritance, as it is said, “each person, according to his number, shall be given his inheritance.” 


Verse 63



Verse 64

<b>Among this [census] there was no man, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>However, against the women, the decree of the spies was not issued, since they cherished the land. The men said, “let us appoint a leader and we will return to Egypt”! <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>while the women said, “give us possession”! This is why the chapter of the daughters of Tzelofchad is adjacent here. 


Chapter 27



Verse 1

<b>Of the families of Menashe the son of Yoseif.</b> Why is this said? Has it not already said “the son of Menashe”? But it teaches you: Yoseif cherished the land, as it is said: “You must carry up my bones up, etc.,” and his daughters cherished the land, as it is said: “Give us possession,”! And <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to teach you, that they were all righteous. For where someone’s deeds, and the deeds of his forefathers, are not defined, and Scripture specifically relates one of them to a virtuous ancestor, then this is a righteous person, the son of a righteous person. If he is related disparagingly, as, for example, “Yishmael, the son of Nesanyah, the son of Elishama,” then it is known that everyone mentioned with him was villainous. 
<b>Machlah, No’ah, etc.</b> Below it says, “Machlah and Sirtzah were. . .” This teaches that they were all equal — the order was, therefore, changed. 

Verse 2

<b>Before Moshe and before Elozor.</b> This teaches that they only stood before them in the fortieth year, after Aharon had died. 
<b>Before Moshe.</b> And afterward before Elozor? Is it possible that Moshe did not know and that Elozor did know? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But, rearrange the passage and expound upon it. This is R’ Yoshiyah’s interpretation. Aba Chanan said in the name of R’ Elozor: “They were seated in the study hall, and they stood before all of them.” 

Verse 3

<b>But he was not, etc.</b> Since they were going to say that he died because of his sin, they needed to say, ‘not the sin of the complainers, nor with Korach's assembly, who incited [the people] against the Holy One, Blessed is He — was he. Rather, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he died by his sin alone, without provoking others to sin with him.’ R’ Akiva said, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”He was the wood gatherer,” R’ Shimon said, “He was <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>among those who ascended defiantly.” 

Verse 4

<b>Why should the name of our father be omitted.</b> We are substitutes for a son. And if females are not considered issue, then let our mother perform levirate marriage with her brother-in-law. 
<b>Because he did not have a son.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But if he had a son, they would not have entered a claim. This teaches <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that they were learned. 

Verse 5

<b>Moshe brought their case.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The halachah was concealed from him. Here he was punished for assuming the crown by saying, “Matters too difficult for you, you may bring before me.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: It was fitting that this chapter be written through Moshe, but the daughters of Tzelofchad were meritorious, and it was written through them. 


Verse 6



Verse 7

<b>Tzelofchad’s daughters speak justly.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As Targum renders, יָאוּת, “correctly.” This chapter is just so inscribed before Me on high. This teaches that their eye discerned what Moshe’s did not. 
<b>Tzelofchad’s daughters speak justly.</b> Their claim was proper. Fortunate is the person with whom the Holy One, Blessed is He, concurs with his words. 
<b>Give [lit. Give, you shall give].</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Two portions. The portion of their father, who was among those who left Egypt, and his portion with his brothers, in the property of Cheifer. 
<b>Transfer.</b> The word הַעֲבַרְתָּ <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>denotes transference (anger), when someone does not leave a son to inherit him. Another interpretation: Because a daughter transfers the inheritance from tribe to tribe, as her son or husband inherit her. The prohibition against transferring an inheritance was placed <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>only on that generation. Similarly, “his hereditary property shall be transferred to his daughter.” With all of them, it says “give,” but with the daughter, it says “transfer.” 

Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11

<b>The the relative closest to him in his family.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Nothing constitutes family except from the father’s side. 


Verse 12

<b>Go up this Avarim Mountain.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Why is this placed here? When the Holy One, Blessed is He, said [to Moshe], “give them. . .,” he said, ‘God commanded me to give them the hereditary property. Perhaps the decree was abrogated, and I may enter the land.’ The Holy One, Blessed is He, said to him, “My decree remains in place.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: When Moshe entered the inheritance given to the sons of Gad and Reuven, he rejoiced, and said, ‘It seems that the vow regarding me was abrogated.’ This is comparable to a king who decreed that his son could not enter the doorway to his palace. He [the King] entered the gateway, and he [the son] followed, [he entered] the courtyard, and he followed, [he entered] the anteroom, and he followed. When he was about to enter <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the chamber, he [the king] said to him, ‘My son, from here and onward, you are forbidden to enter.’ 


Verse 13

<b>As your brother Aharon was gathered.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>From here we derive that Moshe yearned for a death such as Aharon’s. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: You are no better than he. “Because you did not sanctify. . .” But if you had sanctified Me, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>your time would not yet have arrived, for passing from the world. Wherever their death is mentioned, their iniquity is mentioned, because it was decreed that the generation of the wilderness would die in the wilderness, for their sin of not having faith. Moshe, therefore, requested that his iniquity be mentioned, so that it would not be said that he, too, was among those who rebelled. This is comparable to two women who were punished by the court, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>one for degenerate behavior, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the other for eating unripened Shmittah produce, etc. Here, too, wherever their death is mentioned, their iniquity is mentioned, to make it known that there was nothing [sinful] about them but this. 

Verse 14

<b>Those were the waters of dispute at Kadeish.</b> Those alone — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they had no other sins. Another interpretation: Those of <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the rebellion at Marah were the same as those of the rebellion at the Reed Sea, and the very same as those of the rebellion at the desert of Tzin. 


Verse 15

<b>Moshe spoke to Adonoy, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>To make the virtue of the righteous known — when they pass from the world, they ignore their own needs, and concern themselves with the needs of the community. 
<b>Saying.</b> He said to Him, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>‘answer me. Will You appoint a leader over them or not.’ 

Verse 16

<b>Let Adonoy . . . appoint.</b> When Moshe heard the Omnipresent say to him, ‘give Tzelofchad’s inheritance to his daughters,’ <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he said, ‘The time has come for me to ask for a personal request — that my sons may inherit my position of leadership.’ The Holy One, Blessed is He said to him, ‘That is not My intention. Yehoshua is worthy of being rewarded for his service, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as he never moved from the tent. This is [the meaning of] Shlomo’s statement, “he who keeps watch over the fig tree shall eat its fruit.” 
<b>God of the spirits.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Why was this said? He said before Him: “Master of the universe, the thought of every individual is known before you, each dissimilar to the other’s. Appoint a leader over them who will exercise forbearance with each of them according to his intellect.” 

Verse 17

<b>Who will go forth before them.</b> Unlike the approach of the gentile kings, who stay at home and dispatch their armies to war. Rather, as I did, when I battled Sichon and Og, as it is said, “do not fear him,” and the way Yehoshua acted, as it is said, “Yehoshua went to him and said to him, ‘are you ours, etc.”’ Similarly, with David, it says, “for he goes forth and comes before them.” He goes forth at their head, and enters at their head. 
<b>Who will lead them out.</b> With his merit.
<b>And bring them in.</b> With his merit. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation of “and bring them in”: That You will not treat him the way You treat me — for I will not bring them into the land.

Verse 18

<b>Take to yourself.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Take him with words of persuasion — you are fortunate to merit leading the children of the Omnipresent.
<b>Yourself.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Someone scrutinized by you, one whom you recognize. 

<b>In whom there is spirit.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>As you requested, capable of accommodating everyone’s spirit. 
<b>And lay your hand on him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Provide a public announcer for him in order <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that he might preach during your lifetime, so that it should not be said of him that he was unable to lift his head in Moshe’s day. 


Verse 19

<b>And command him.</b> Concerning the Bnei Yisroel. Know that they are tedious and recalcitrant — [your appointment is] on condition that you accept this.

Verse 20

<b>Bestow some of your radiance on him.</b> This refers to radiance of the facial skin.
<b>Some of your radiance.</b> But not all your radiance. Hence we learn that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the face of Moshe was like the sun, the face of Yehoshua like the moon. 
<b>So that the entire community of Bnei Yisroel will hear.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They will treat him with reverence and awe, the way they treat you. 


Verse 21

<b>He shall stand before Elozor the <i>kohein.</i></b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Here is [the reply to] your request — this glory will not be removed from your father’s house, as Yehoshua, too, will depend on the affirmation of Elozor. 
<b>And ask, of him.</b> When he needs to go to war. 
<b>By his word.</b> [the word] of Elozor.
<b>And the entire community.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The Sanhedrin.

Verse 22

<b>He took Yehoshua.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He persuaded him, verbally, informing him of the reward for the leaders of Klal Yisroel in the World to Come. 


Verse 23

<b>He laid his hands.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Generously, over and above what he had been commanded. For the Holy One, Blessed is He, said to him, “lay your hand,” but he used both hands. He fashioned him like a vessel filled to overflowing, filling him generously with his wisdom. 
<b>As Adonoy had commanded.</b> also regarding the radiance — He bestowed some of his radiance on him.

Chapter 28



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>Command Bnei Yisroel.</b> What is stated above? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”May God command. . .” The Holy One, Blessed is He, said to him, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>‘Before you command Me concerning My children, command My children concerning Me.’ This is comparable to a princess who was passing from the world. She instructed her husband concerning her children, etc., as is stated in Sifri. 
<b>My offering.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This refers to the blood.
<b>My bread.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This refers to the “<i>emurin</i>” parts, as it is said, “The <i>kohein</i> shall burn them on the altar, bread of the fire.” 
<b>Of My fires.</b> to be placed on the fires of My altar.
<b>You shall be vigilant.</b> The <i>kohanim,</i> Levites and Bnei Yisroel shall stand over it. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They learned from here, and instituted the “<i>ma’amados</i>” units. 
<b>At its prescribed time.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Every day is the time prescribed for the constant-offerings.

Verse 3

<b>Say to them.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is an admonishment to the <i>Bais Din</i>.
<b>Two each day.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like the plain interpretation, but essentially, it teaches <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that they should be slaughtered towards the sun, the constant morning sacrifice to the west, and that of the afternoon <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to the east of the rings. 

Verse 4

<b>One lamb.</b> Although it is already stated in the <i>parasha</i> of “You shall command” — “this is what you shall offer,” — those instructions were for the days of inauguration, whereas <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>here, the commandment is for all the generations. 

Verse 5

<b>Fine flour as a meal-offering.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The libation <i>minchah.</i>

Verse 6

<b>As offered on Mount Sinai.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like those which were done during the days of inauguration. Another interpretation [of] which was done at Mount Sinai: The constant burnt-offering is compared to the burnt-offering at Mount Sinai — the one brought before the giving of the Torah — of which Scripture states “. . .and [he] placed it in the basins.” This teaches that it (the constant-offering) requires a vessel.

Verse 7

<b>Its libation.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Wine.
<b>In the Holy [Sanctuary], you shall pour.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They shall be poured on the altar. 
<b>An intoxicating libation.</b> Intoxicating wine. This excludes wine, fresh from the wine press. 

Verse 8

<b>A pleasing aroma.</b> It pleases Me that I spoke and My wish was fulfilled.

Verse 9



Verse 10

<b>This is the burnt-offering on its Shabbos.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But not one Shabbos burnt-offering on another Shabbos. Suppose it was not offered on this Shabbos, I might think that two should be offered on the following Shabbos. The Torah therefore teaches “on its Shabbos.” This informs us that once its day has passed, the offering expires. 
<b>In addition to the constant (daily) burnt-offering.</b> This refers to the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices, aside from the two constant burnt-offering lambs. This teaches that they (the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices) may be brought only <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>between the two constant-offerings. Similarly, concerning all the <i>musaf</i> sacrifices it is said, “in addition to the constant burnt-offering,” for this teaching. 


Verse 11



Verse 12

<b>Three tenths [of an <i>eiphah</i>].</b> As specified for the libations of a bull, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>designated as such in the chapter of the libations. 

Verse 13



Verse 14

<b>This is the burnt-offering of each [Rosh] Chodesh, at its renewal.</b> But once its designated day has passed, the offering expires, with no provision for restitution. 


Verse 15

<b>And one he-goat, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>All the <i>musaf</i> goats came in atonement for <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the ritual defilement of the Sanctuary and its sacred objects, everything as explained in Tractate Shevuos. There is a distinction with the New Moon goat, for it is said, concerning it, “. . .to God.” This teaches you that it atones for someone <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>who was not cognizant either at the beginning or the end, as no one recognizes the transgression save for the Holy One, Blessed is He, alone. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The other goats are derived from this one. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is also expounded <i>aggadically</i> [as follows]: The Holy One, Blessed is He, said: ‘Bring atonement for Me, because I diminished the moon.’ 
<b>In addition to the constant (daily) burnt-offering, it shall be done.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This entire offering. 

<b>And its libation.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”Its libation” does not relate to the goat, as a sin-offering has no libation. 

Verse 16



Verse 17



Verse 18

<b>Any work of consequence.</b> Even work necessary for you, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for example, to prevent a loss, which is permitted during the intermediary holiday, is prohibited during the festival. 

Verse 19

<b>Bulls.</b> Corresponding with Avraham, as it is said, “Avraham ran to the cattle.” 
<b>Ram.</b> Corresponding with the ram of Yitzchok.
<b>Sheep.</b> Corresponding with Yaakov, as it is said, “Yaakov separated the lambs.” I saw this in R’ Moshe Hadarshan’s commentary. 

Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24

<b>Like these, yoshall make daily.</b> They should not be progressively decreasing like the oxen of the [<i>Succos</i>] festival. 

Verse 25



Verse 26

<b>On the day of the first fruits.</b> The Shavuos festival is called “[The festival of] the first fruits of the wheat harvest,” because of the offering of the two loaves, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>which are the first of the wheat <i>minchah</i>-offerings to come from the new crop. 


Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31

<b>[The sacrifices] shall be without blemish — and their libations.</b> The libations must also be unblemished. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The Rabbis derive from this that wine in which floury decay globules have surfaced is disqualified for libations. 


Chapter 29



Verse 1



Verse 2



Verse 3



Verse 4



Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>Aside from the [Rosh] Chodesh burnt- offering. </b> The [Rosh] Chodesh <i>Musaf</i>- offerings, as it (the new moon) corresponds with the new year. 


Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11

<b>Aside from the atonement sin-offering.</b> The goat offered in the inner chamber, mentioned in “Acharei Mos.” It, too, was a sin- offering. 
<b>And the constant (daily) burnt- offering</b> And <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>aside from the constant burnt- offering, you shall offer these burnt-offerings. 
<b>And their libations.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This relates to the <i>musaf</i>-offerings stated above, and to “you shall offer.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>It denotes a command: ‘Aside from the constant burnt-offering and its <i>minchah,</i> you shall offer these and their libations.’ It is the same with every “their libations” said at all the festivals, except those concerning the [<i>Succos</i>] holiday sacrifices. Every “and its libation,” “and their libations,” “and its libations” among them refer to the constant sacrifice, and are not commands, since the <i>musaf</i> libations are written separately for each day. 


Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16



Verse 17



Verse 18

<b>Their meal-offerings and their libations for the bulls.</b> There were seventy festival bulls, representing the seventy nations, which were progressively diminishing, symbolizing their destruction. During the time of the Sanctuary, [however,] These sacrifices shielded them from suffering. 
<b>And the lambs.</b> Representing Israel, which is called “the dispersed lamb.” Their numbers are constant, and they total ninety eight, to nullify the ninety eight curses in Mishneh Torah. On the second day, וְנִסְכֵּיהֶם, “and their libations,” is said, in relation to the day’s two constant-offerings. The change in language was intended for exposition, as the Rabbis, of blessed memory, remarked: On the second day, וְנִסְכֵּיהֶם, “and their libations,” is said, on the sixth, וּנְסָכֶיהָ, “and her libations,” on the seventh, כְּמִשְׁפָּטָם, “according to ‘their’ requirement.” מ"ם, יו"ד, מ"ם . which spells מַּיִם, “water,” and is an allusion that the water libation, during the Festival is Scriptural. 


Verse 19



Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24



Verse 25



Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32



Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35

<b>Shall be a [day of] restraint for you.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Restraint from doing work. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpetation [of] restraint, restrain yourselves from leaving. This teaches that they were required to remain overnight. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>According to the Aggadic Midrash, because, throughout the entire holiday, they brought offerings which represented the seventy nations. When they were going to leave, the Omnipresent said to them, ‘I request of you, make a small repast for me, so that I may enjoy your company.’ 


Verse 36

<b>One young bull, one ram.</b> These <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>represent Yisroel [which is singular to the Holy One, Blessed is He] — ‘Remain with Me a little longer’. This denotes affection, as when children take leave of their father, and he says to them, ‘Your departure distresses me, remain yet another day’. This is compared to a king who made a repast, etc., as stated in tractate Succah. Midrash R’ Tanchumah interprets: The Torah teaches <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>proper conduct. Someone who entertains a guest should, on the first day, feed him fattened fowl, the next day fish, the next beef, the next day he should feed him grains, and the next, vegetables. Progressive diminishment, like the festival bulls. 

Verse 37



Verse 38



Verse 39

<b>These you shall make to Adonoy on your festivals.</b> Those things designated <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>as obligations.
<b>Aside from your vows.</b> If you should decide to vow offerings during the holiday, this will be credited to you as a commendable act. Or, the vows and gifts which you pledged throughout the year, bring during the holiday, as it may be difficult for you to make the return pilgrimage to Jerusalem to offer up your pledges, and you may thus ultimately violate the prohibition of “. . .do not delay [fulfilling your pledge].” 

Chapter 30



Verse 1

<b>Moshe spoke to Bnei Yisroel.</b> This concludes the subject, comments R’ Yishmael. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Because, up until this point, we have the words of the Omnipresent, and the chapter of vows begins with the words of Moshe, it is necessary to conclude the subject by saying that Moshe reviewed this <i>parshah</i> with the Israelites. Otherwise, the implication would be that he (Moshe) did not tell them this, but began his discourse with the chapter of vows. 


Verse 2

<b>The tribal leaders.</b> He bestowed honor on the leaders <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>by teaching them first, and afterward, all of Bnei Yisroel. How do we know that the other discourses were so? The Torah therefore teaches, “. . . they returned to him— Aharon and all the leaders of the congregation— and Moshe spoke to them. Afterward, all of Bnei Yisroel approached.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Why, then, did he see fit to say this here? He taught that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>vows may be nullified by a single expert. When there is no single expert, nullification is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>by three laymen. But perhaps Moshe recited this chapter <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>only to the leaders? “This is the word” is said here, and it is said concerning slaughtering outside [the Temple], “this is the word.” Just as that was said to Aharon and his sons, and all of Bnei Yisroel, as it is said, “speak to Aharon, etc.,” so was this, said to all of them. 
<b>This is the word.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Moshe prophesied with “this is what Adonoy has said, about the time of midnight. . .,” and the [other] prophets prophesied with “this is what Adonoy has said:” Moshe surpassed them, as he prophesied <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>with the phrase “this is the word.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Another interpretation: “This is the word” is exclusionary, teaching that <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the Sage [annuls] with the term “release,” and the husband with the term “nullification,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>following the Scriptural language here. If they reverse the terminology, there is neither release nor nullification. 

Verse 3

<b>A vow.</b> By saying, ‘Let it be as <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>a <i>konam</i> to me, that I will not eat, or I may not do a certain thing.’ But perhaps, even if he swears to eat the meat of an animal that was not ritually slaughtered, I read, concerning him, “all that he has verbalized, he must fulfill”? The Torah, therefore, teaches, “. . .to initiate a prohibition”— to prohibit what is permitted, but not to permit what is prohibited. 
<b>He may not profane his word.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like Gא יְחַלֵּל דְבָרוֹ, he may not secularize his word. 

Verse 4

<b>In her father’s home.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Under her father’s jurisdiction, even if she is not actually in his home. 
<b>While still in her youth.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But not a minor, or a “<i>bogeres,</i>” as a minor’s vows are invalid, and a <i>bogeres</i> is no longer under her father’s jurisdiction for nullification of vows. When is she considered a minor? Our Rabbis say, at the age of eleven and a day, her vows should be examined. If she recognizes in Who’s Name she took the vow, or in Who’s Name she made the sanctification, then her vow is valid. At the age of twelve and a day, examination is no longer required. 

Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>But if her father restrained her.</b> He restrained her from the vow, in other words, he nullified it. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>I would not know what this הֲנָאָה means, but when it says, “but if, on the day her husband hears about it, יָנִיא אוֹתָהּ וְהֵפֵר, he restrains her and nullifies,” you may conclude that הֲנָאָה means nullification. Its plain meaning is to restrain and turn aside. Similarly, “why do you turn [the people’s hearts] away,” and “let the oil on my head not turn my head,” and “you will know My turning aside” [i.e. the punishment] for turning away from Me.” 

<b>Adonoy will forgive her.</b> To whom does Scripture refer? To a woman who took the Nazirite vow. Her husband heard and nullified it, but she was not aware. She then violated her vow by drinking wine and defiling herself by contact with a corpse. She is in need of forgiveness, although it was nullified. Now, if those who[se vows] have been nullified require forgiveness, certainly those who[se vows] have not been nullified. 


Verse 7

<b>If she is [married] to a man.</b> This refers to an “<i>arusah.</i>” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But perhaps to a “<i>nesuah?</i>” When it says, “and if she took the vow in her husband’s home,” a “<i>nesuah</i>” is mentioned, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>so this must mean an “<i>arusah.</i>” It is intended to distinguish her, in <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that her father and her husband annul her vow. If the father annulled, but not the husband, or the husband, but not the father, there is no annulment, and it goes without saying, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>if one of them endorsed it. 
<b>And her vows were upon herself.</b> She took the vows in her father’s home, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>but her father did not hear them — they were neither annulled <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>nor endorsed. 

Verse 8

<b>And her husband heard, etc.</b> Here you have [the ruling] that if the husband endorses, it stands. 

Verse 9

<b>He then annuls her vow which was upon her.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Perhaps even if the father did not annul? The Torah therefore teaches, “in her youth, while in her father’s house” — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>all through her youth, she is under her father’s jurisdiction. 

Verse 10

<b>Everything she prohibited for herself shall remain incumbent upon her.</b> Since she is neither under the jurisdiction of the father, nor the jurisdiction of the husband. Scripture refers here to <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>a widow after “<i>nisuin,</i>” but a widow after “<i>erusin,</i>” when the husband dies, his jurisdiction transfers to the father. 

Verse 11

<b>But if she took the vow in her husband’s home.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Scripture refers to a “<i>nesuah.</i>”

Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14

<b>Every vow, and every oath of self-denial, etc.</b> Since it was said that the husband may annul, perhaps all vows are included; the Torah therefore teaches, “of self-denial.” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He may only annul vows which are of self-denial They are defined in tractate Nedarim. 

Verse 15

<b>From one day to the next.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>So that you should not say [he may annul] for twenty four hours — this is why “from day to day” is said, to teach that he may only annul <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>until nightfall. 

Verse 16

<b>After having heard.</b> After he heard and endorsed, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>saying, “I approve,” he recanted and annuled it, even during the same day. 
<b>He must bear her transgression.</b> He must take her place. We learn from here that one who causes another’s downfall, must bear full punishment in his place. 


Chapter 31



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>Against the Midianites.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But not against the Moavites, for the Moavites entered the matter out of fear. They were afraid of them, [fearing] that they would plunder them, as it only says, “do not provoke them with warfare.” The Midianites, however, were <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>enraged over a dispute which was not theirs. Another interpretation: <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for the sake of two virtuous doves whom I must extract from them — Rus the Moavite, and Na’amah the Ammonite. 
 

Verse 3

<b>Moshe spoke, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Although he heard that his demise depended on the matter, he joyfully implemented it, without delay. 
<b>Arm.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, meaning the same as חֲלוּצֵי צָבָא, “armed.” 
<b>Men.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Righteous men. Similarly, “choose men for us,” and, “men who are wise and renowned.”
