<b>Revenge of Adonoy.</b> For, when anyone stands against Yisroel, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>it is as if he stands against the Holy One, Blessed is He. 

Verse 4

<b>For all of the tribes of Yisroel.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This includes the tribe of Levi.

Verse 5

<b>They were handed over.</b> This informs you of the praiseworthiness of the shepherds of Yisroel, of how cherished they are by Yisroel. Before they heard about his death, what did he say? “a while more and they will stone me”! Yet, when they heard that the death of Moshe depended on the vengeance against Midian, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they refused to go until they were handed over, against their wishes. 

Verse 6

<b>Them, and Pinchas.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This teaches that Pinchas was equivalent to all of them. But <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>why did Pinchas go, while Elozor did not? The Holy One, Blessed is He, said, “The one who began the <i>mitzvah</i> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>by executing Kozbi, the daughter of Tzur, should complete it.” Another interpretation: He sought to avenge Yoseif, his maternal forefather, as it is said, “the Midianites sold him. . .” How is it derived that the mother of Pinchas was [descended] from Yoseif? Since it is said, “of the daughters of Putiel (פּוּטִיאֵל).” Of the children of Yisro, who fattened (פִּיטֵם) calves for idol worship, and of the children of Yoseif, who scorned (פִּטְפֵּט) his evil inclination. Another interpretation: He was annointed for warfare. 
<b>With the sacred vessels.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This refers to the Ark and the Golden Headplate. Because Bil’am accompanied them, and caused the Midianite kings to fly through sorcery, he himself flying with them, he [Pinchas] displayed the Golden Headplate to them, in which the Divine Name was engraved, and they fell. This is why it is said, “. . .on those they had slain,” concerning the Midianite kings — they fell from the air on the slain ones. Similarly, concerning Bil’am, it is written, “. . .upon those they had slain” in the book of Yehoshua. 
<b>In his hand.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>In his possession. Similarly, “he took his entire country מִיָדוֹ, from his possession.” 


Verse 7



Verse 8

<b>[The] five kings of Midian.</b> Can I not see that Scripture enumerates five? Why, then, is it necessary to say “five”? Evidently, to teach that they all conspired equally, and they were all punished equally. Bil’am went there <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to receive the reward for the twenty-four thousand whom he felled from Yisroel, through his advice. He went from Midian to the Bnei Yisroel, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and offered them evil advice. he said to them, “If when you were six hundred thousand you could not overcome them, and now you intend to fight them with twelve thousand?’ They gave him <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>his reward, in full without stinting. 
<b>With the sword.</b> He set upon Yisroel, exchanging his craft for theirs. For they are only victorious through verbal expression, through prayer and supplication. He came and took up their craft, to curse them verbally. So they confronted him as well by exchanging their craft for that of the gentiles, who come with the sword, as it is said, “you shall live by your sword.” 

Verse 9



Verse 10

<b>Their palaces.</b> The place of their guardians. The word (טִירֹתָם) denoting dwelling places for monks proficient in their laws. Another interpretation: The word denotes dwelling places for their ministers, as Targum renders “the P’lishtite <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>ministers,” טוּרְנֵי פְלִשְׁתָּאֵי . 

Verse 11

<b>They took all the booty, etc.</b> This teaches that they were conscientious and righteous, beyond suspicion of theft through confiscating the booty without permission, as it is said, all the booty, etc. Concerning them, Scriptural tradition states explicitly, “your teeth are like a flock of sheep, etc.” — even the warriors among you are all righteous. 
<b>Booty.</b> This refers to moveable property consisting of clothing and ornaments.
<b>Plunder.</b> [Refers to] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>plunder of moveable property, that is non-ornamental. 
<b>All that had been seized.</b> Men and beasts. When “captives” is written next to “spoils,” then “captives” refers to men, and “spoils” to beasts. 


Verse 12



Verse 13

<b>Moshe and Elozor the kohein went out.</b> Because they saw the Israelite youths going out to seize some of the plunder.

Verse 14

<b>Moshe was angry with the commanders of the army.</b> Who were appointed over the army. This teaches that the entire corruption of the generation is attributed to the great men, since they have the power to rebuke. 

Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>They were the very same ones.</b> This informs us that they recognized them — “this is the one through which so-and-so had his downfall.”
<b>On Bil’am’s advice.</b> He said to them, “Even if you gather together all the multitudes of the world, you will be unable to conquer them. Perhaps you are more numerous than the Egyptians, who had six hundred choice chariots? Come, I shall advise you. Their god despises promiscuity, etc.,’ as stated in “Chelek,” and in Sifri. 

Verse 17

<b>And every woman with intimate knowledge of a man.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Capable of intimate relations, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>even if she never actually had relations. They brought them before the Golden Headplate — and those capable of relations — their faces turned sickly green. 
<b>You shall execute.</b> Why is this repeated? To separate the matter— these are R’ Yishmael’s remarks. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>For, when I read, “execute every male among the children, and every woman with intimate knowledge of a man, and all the children among the females, etc.,” I do not know [concerning every woman with intimate knowledge of a man] whether to execute [them] with the males, or allow them to live with the children. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This is why “[you must] execute” is said. 

Verse 18



Verse 19

<b>Outside the camp.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>So that they would not enter the Sanctuary courtyard.
<b>Whoever has killed a person.</b> R’ Meir said, “Scripture refers to a person who kills with an object capable of receiving contamination, and Scripture teaches <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that a utensil defiles a person when it is in contact with a corpse as if he had touched the corpse itself. Or, perhaps even if he shot an arrow at him and killed him? The Torah, therefore, teaches, “and whoever touched a corpse.” It compares one who kills with one who touches. Just as the one who touches (receives contamination) through contact, so does the one who kills (receives contamination) through contact.” 
<b>Purify yourselves.</b> With sprinkling water, as prescribed for others who were defiled by contact with the dead. For, even those who rule that Gentile graves do not convey contamination in a tent, — as it is said, “you, my sheep, my pastoral sheep, you are man”; you are entitled “man,” he admits that gentiles convey contamination through touching and carrying. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Since “man” was only said in the context of tent contamination, as it is said, “a person who dies in a tent.” 
<b>You and your captives.</b> Not that the gentiles receive contamination and require sprinkling. Rather, just as you are members of the convenant, so with your captives, when they enter the covenant — should they become contaminated, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>they will require sprinkling. 

Verse 20

<b>Everything made of goat products.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This includes utensils made from the horns, hoofs, and bones. 

Verse 21

<b>Elozor the <i>kohein</i> said, etc.</b> Because Moshe fell into a state of anger, he fell into a state of error, so concealed from him, were the laws concerning purging the utensils of gentiles. You find a similarity on the eighth day of inauguration, as it is said, “he was angry with Elozor and with Isamar”— he fell into a state of anger, [and] he fell into a state or error. Similarly with “listen, now, rebels”! “he struck the rock.” Because of anger, he erred. 

<b>Which Adonoy commanded, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He credited the teaching to his master. 

Verse 22

<b>Only the gold, etc.</b> Although Moshe did not warn you except for the laws of ritual uncleanliness, you must be warned further, concerning the laws of purging. “Only” denotes exclusion, as if to say, ‘you are excluded from using the utensils, even after their purification from contamination by the dead, until they are purified from the absorption of forbidden “<i>neveilah</i>” meat.’ Our Rabbis remark that “only the gold, etc.” teaches that one must remove its rust before purging it. This is the connotation of the word “only” — there should be no rust there, only the metal, exactly as it is. 

Verse 23

<b>Anything placed on a fire.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>In which to cook something.
<b>You must pass through fire.</b> It must be purged the way it was used. Something used with heated water, one purges with heated water; something used for roasting, like a spit or a grill, one brings to white heat with fire. 
<b>However, it must be purified with sprinkling water.</b> According to the plain interpretation, this purification is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to cleanse it from the contamination of the dead. He said to them, ‘The utensils require purging to purify them from prohibited food, and purification, to cleanse them from ritual contamination.’ And the Rabbis extrapolate here, that even for purification from prohibited [food contamination], metal utensils require immersion, and מֵי נִדָּה written here they expound as referring to water suitable for the immersion of the “<i>niddah.</i>” How much is this? Forty <i>seah.</i> 
<b>But anything that was not placed on a fire.</b> Anything not used with fire, such as cups [and jugs], and flasks, which are used for cold food, and, therefore, did not absorb prohibited [food]. 
<b>You may pass through water.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Immerse them, and it is sufficient. This is only with metal utensils. 

Verse 24

<b>Into the camp.</b> To the camp of the <i>Shechinah</i> [only], for someone contaminated by the dead need not be banished from the camp of the Levites and the camp of the Israelites. 

Verse 25



Verse 26

<b>Take count (lit. count the heads).</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Make an accounting.

Verse 27

<b>Divide in half the spoils seized among those who took the war in hand, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Half for these, and half for these. 


Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32

<b>The spoil was — in addition to the booty.</b> Because they were not commanded to contribute the tax from the moveable property, but from the spoil, the phrase was written this way. ‘the spoil, which would be included in the distribution and included in the tax, which remained after the plunder of personal property that the warriors plundered for themselves without distributing — [that spoil] was; the number of sheep, etc.’ 


Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36



Verse 37



Verse 38



Verse 39



Verse 40



Verse 41



Verse 42

<b>From the half [designated] for Bnei Yisroel that Moshe divided.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>For the community, by appropriating it for them from the military men. 

Verse 43

<b>The community’s half consisted of.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>So much and so much.

Verse 44



Verse 45



Verse 46



Verse 47

<b>Moshe took, etc.</b>

Verse 48

<b>The officers.</b> Those who were appointed.

Verse 49

<b> וְלֹא־נִפְקַד . Not [a man is] missing.</b> Targum [Onkelos] renders לֹא שְׁגָא . This (שְׁגָא), too, denotes, in Aramaic, “missing,” like “I [will suffer] its loss,” rendered by Targum, דַּהֲוָת שָׁגְיָא מִמִּנְיָנָא, “whatever is missing from the tally.” Similarly, “for your seat will be missing” — your seating place will be missing, the one who usually sits there. Similarly, “ וַיִפָּקֵד מְקוֹם דָּוִד,” his place was missing — and no one was sitting there. 


Verse 50

<b>Anklet.</b> This refers to leg bands.
<b>Bracelet.</b> On the arm.
<b>Ring.</b> Ear rings.
<b>Clasp.</b> Shaped around the crotch, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to atone for their sinful thoughts concerning the daughters of Midian. 

Chapter 32



Verse 1



Verse 2



Verse 3

<b>Ataros, Divon, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They were part of the land of Sichon and Og. 


Verse 4



Verse 5



Verse 6

<b>Should your brothers.</b> This denotes a question.

Verse 7

<b>Why do you dishearten.</b> Turn aside and restrain their hearts from crossing, for they will think that you are afraid to cross because of the war, and the strength of the cities and the people. 


Verse 8

<b>From Kadeish Barnei’a.</b> This was its name. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>There were two places named Kadeish.

Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11



Verse 12

<b>The Kenizite.</b> He was Kaleiv’s stepfather, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to whom Kaleiv’s mother bore Osniel. 

Verse 13

<b>He made them wander.</b> He moved them about, as in “a wanderer and vagrant” 

Verse 14

<b>To add.</b> As in “add a year to a year,” “add your burnt-offerings, etc.” The word denotes addition. 


Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>We will build [enclosures] for our flocks here.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They were more concerned over their property than [over] their sons and daughters, for they gave precedence to their flocks over their children. Moshe said to them, ‘not so! Treat what is of major importance as such, and what is secondary as such. First build yourselves cities for your children, and afterward pens for your flocks.’ 

Verse 17

<b>We will then arm ourselves rapidly.</b> We will arm ourselves quickly, as in “quicken the spoil, hasten the plunder,” “let him hurry, hasten [his actions].” 
<b>Before Bnei Yisroel.</b> At the head of the armies, since they were great warriors, as it is said concerning Gad, “he shall tear arms, skulls as well.” Moshe, too, reiterated specifically to them, in “These are the words”: “I commanded you at that time, etc., go forth armed before your brothers, Bnei Yisroel, all [you] great warriors.” And at Yericho it is written, “the armed force went before them” — they were [the sons of] Reuven and Gad, who fulfilled their condition. 
<b>Our children will dwell.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>When we are with our brothers.
<b>In fortified cities.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Which we shall build now.

Verse 18



Verse 19

<b>Across the Yardein and beyond.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>On the western bank.
<b>For, our inheritance came to us.</b> We have already received it, on the eastern bank. 

Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24

<b>For your sheep.</b> This word is <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>conjugated from 'צֹנֶה', “all the sheep and cattle.” It does not have the “ אָלֶ"ף “ intervening between the “ נוּ"ן “ and “ צָדִ"י “ and the “ אָלֶ"ף “ which appears here after the “ נּוּ"ן “ is instead of the “ הֵ"א “ of צֹנֶה . I learned this from R’ Moshe Hadarshan’s commentary. 
<b>But what you have expressed verbally,</b> you must fulfill. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>For the sake of Heaven, as you pledged to cross and do battle until the conquest and apportionment [of the land]. Moshe had only requested of them, “the land will be conquered, etc. and after you may return” but they pledged “until [Bnei Yisroel] have inherited” — so they added that they would remain for the seven years of apportionment, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and they did so. 

Verse 25

<b>The tribe of Gad said.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>All of them as one man. 


Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28

<b>[Moshe] commanded, to them.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like עֲלֵיהֶם, concerning them and their stipulation, he appointed Elozor and Yehoshua, as in “God will fight for you.” 


Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32

<b>And we shall [then] have our permanent inheritance.</b> As if to say, ‘in our hands, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in our possession, will be our hereditary territory on this side.’ 


Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36

<b>Fortified cities and sheep pens.</b> The end of this passage is related to the begning ofhe subject — “the sons of Gad built” these cities, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to serve as fortified cities and sheep pens. 

Verse 37



Verse 38

<b>Nevo, Ba’al Me’on, their names having been changed.</b> Nevo and Ba’al Meon were names of idols. The Emorites <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>would name their cities after their idols, so the sons of Reuven changed their names in favor of other names. This is the meaning of “their names having been changed” — Nevo and Ba’al Me’on were turned aside in favor of a different name. 
<b>And Sivmah.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They built Sivmah. This is Sevam mentioned above.

Verse 39

<b>And drove out.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, וְתָרִיךְ, “and ousted,” for the word יָרֹשׁ may be used in two ways, to denote inheritance, or to denote ousting, meaning driving out, expelling. 

Verse 40



Verse 41

<b>Villages.</b> כַּפְרְנֵיהוֹן, their villages. 
<b>And [he] called them Chavos Yair.</b> Because he had no children, he called them by his name, as a memorial. 

Verse 42

<b>And [he] called it Novach.</b> לָה does not have a dot in its ה . I saw in R’ Moshe Hadarshan’s commentary: Because this name did not endure, it is therefore silent, implying that it is to be expounded as לָא, “not” [Novach]. But I wonder <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>how he (R’ Moshe) would expound two similar words, וַיֹאמֶר 'לָה' בֹעַז, “Boaz said to her,” לִבְנוֹת לָה בַיִת, “to build her a house.” 


Chapter 33



Verse 1

<b>These are the journeys.</b> Why were these journeys recorded? To make the Omnipresent’s benevolence known. For, although He decreed to move them about and cause them to wander in the wilderness, do not say that they wandered and were moved about from journey to journey all forty years, and had no rest — for there are only forty two journeys here. Subtract fourteen, all of which took place during the first year, before the decree, from their journey from Ra’meses until they reached Rismah, from where the spies were dispatched, as it is said, “after, the people journeyed from Chatzeros, etc. Send, for yourself, men, etc.,” and here it says, “they journeyed from Chatzeros and camped at Rismah,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>you learn that it was in the desert of Paran. Exclude, further, from there, eight journeys which took place after Aharon’s death, from Mount Hor to the plains of Moav, during the fortieth year, it is found <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that throughout the thirty eight years, they took only twenty journeys. This is from R’ Moshe [Hadarshan]’s commentary. R’ Tanchuma <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>expounds the matter differently: This is compared to a king whose son was ill, and he brought him to a distant place for treatment. When they returned, the father began enumerating all the journeys. He said to him, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”Here, we slept; here, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>we were chilled; here, your head ached, etc.’ 


Verse 2



Verse 3



Verse 4

<b>Egypt was burying.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>They were preoccupied with their grief. 


Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11



Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15



Verse 16



Verse 17



Verse 18

<b>And camped in Rismoh.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>So named after the spies’ slander, as it is said, “what will He (God) give you, and what more will He add for you, O deceitful tongue? Sharpened warrior’s arrows, with smoldering coals.” 


Verse 19



Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24



Verse 25



Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29



Verse 30



Verse 31



Verse 32



Verse 33



Verse 34



Verse 35



Verse 36



Verse 37



Verse 38

<b>By the word [lit. mouth] of Adonoy.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This teaches that he died by the Divine kiss.

Verse 39



Verse 40

<b>The Cannanite heard.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>This teaches you that the death of Aharon was the news he heard that the clouds of glory had departed, and he (the Canaanite) thought that it was permissible to wage war against the Israelites. This is why Scripture repeats it. 


Verse 41



Verse 42



Verse 43



Verse 44

<b>At the ruins of Avarim.</b> The word [עִיֵּי] denotes desolation and waste, as in, “. . . into a desolate field,” “they have turned Yerushalayim into desolation.” 

Verse 45



Verse 46



Verse 47



Verse 48



Verse 49

<b>From Beis Yeshimos until Aveil Hasheetim.</b> Here it teaches you <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the measure of the Israelite camp [was] twelve <i>mils,</i> for Rava, the son of Bar Chana, said, “I have seen that place, etc.” 
<b>Aveil Hasheetim.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The plain of Sheetim was entitled “Aveil.” 


Verse 50



Verse 51

<b>When you cross the Yardein, etc. You must drive out, etc.</b> Were they not admonished several times concerning this? But this is what Moshe said to them: “When you cross the Yardein on dry land, you must cross on this condition, and if you do not, the waters will come and inundate you.” We find that Yehoshua spoke to them similarly while they were still in the Yardein. 

Verse 52

<b>You must drive out.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>You shall oust. 

<b>Their carved stones.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, בֵּית סִגְדַּתְהוֹן, “their houses of worship,” so named because they would overlay the ground with a marblestone floor <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>on which to prostrate themselves with arms and legs extended, as it is written, “overlaid stones you shall not place, in your land, on which to prostrate yourselves.” 
<b>Their cast.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, מַתְּכַתְהוֹן, “their molten.” 


Verse 53

<b>Drive out [the inhabitants of] the land.</b> Make it vacant <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>of its inhabitants, and then “you shall dwell in it” — <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>you shall be able to endure there, but if not, you shall be unable to endure there. 


Verse 54

<b>To whomever the lottery [system] ordains.</b> This is a shortened passage, [meaning] “whichever ‘plot’ the lot indicates, shall belong to him’.” 
<b>According to your paternal tribes.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Taking into account those who came out of Egypt. Another interpretation: <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>With twelve border demarcations, following the number of tribes. 


Verse 55

<b>Those whom you will leave over.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Shall be evil to you.
<b>As spikes in your eyes.</b> As spikes which will gouge your eyes out. Targum [Onkelos] renders “spikes” שִׂיכַּיָא .
<b>And thorns.</b> The linguists construe this as <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>denoting a barrier of thorns, which will enclose you, locking and confining you without exit or entrance. 
<b>And they will persecute you.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders. 


Chapter 34



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>This is the land which will fall to you, etc.</b> Since many commandments apply in the land, but do not apply outside the land, it was necessary to record <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the outer reaches of the borders of its perimeter, to inform you that within those borders, the commandments apply. 
<b>Will fall to you.</b> Because it was apportioned by lot, the apportionment is described <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>in terms of falling. Midrash Aggadah remarks, because the Holy One, Blessed is He, caused the fall of the [celestial] ministers of the seven nations from heaven, and prostrated them before Moshe, and said to him, “observe, they no longer have any power.” 

Verse 3

<b>Your southern flank shall be.</b> The southern side, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>from east to west. 
<b>From the Tzin wilderness.</b> Which adjoining Edom, begins the <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>southeastern corner of the land of the nine tribes. How is this? <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Three countries lie south of Eretz Yisroel, each adjoining the next; part of the land of Egypt, all of the land of Edom, and all of the land of Moav. The land of Egypt is at the southwestern corner, as it is said in this <i>Parshah,</i> “[the border turns] from Atzmon to the Egyptian Estuary and its outskirts shall reach the sea.” The Egyptian Estuary’s path faced the entire land of Egypt, as it is said, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”from the [river] Shichor, facing Egypt,” and separates the land of Egypt from Eretz Yisroel. The land of Edom adjoined it eastward, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>with the land of Moav <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>adjoining the land of Edom at the eastern end of the southern border. When the Bnei Yisroel left Egypt, had the Omnipresent desired to hasten their entry into the land, He would have brought them northward across the Nile, and they would have entered Eretz Yisroel — but He did not do so. This is the meaning of what is said, “God did not lead them along the route of the land of the P’lishtim,” who dwelt by the sea, on the western border of the land of Canaan, as is said concerning the P’lishtim, “those who dwell on the territory by the sea, the Kereisite nation.” He did not lead them along that route, but diverted them, bringing them out by the southern route, into the wilderness — the Yechezkel called “the wilderness of nations,” because several nations dwelt alongside it. He then led them in the south from west to east, continuously, until they reached south of the land of Edom. They requested that the king of Edom permit them to enter his land, traverse its width, and enter the land, but he refused, so they had to travel around the entire southern side of Edom, until they reached south of the land of Moav, as it is said, “he also sent emissaries to the king of Moav, but he refused.” They traveled along the entire southern side of Moav, to the end. From there they turned their faces to the north, until they traveled around its entire eastern border along its width. When they completed its eastern side, they came upon the territory of Sichon and Og, who dwelt east of the land of Canaan, with the Yardein interposing between them. This is the meaning of what was said by Yiftach, “they traveled in the wilderness, proceeded around the land of Edom and the land of Moav, and came to [the end of] the eastern border of the land of Moav.” They conquered the territory of Sichon and Og, which was north of the land of Moav, and came abreast of the Yardein, opposite the northwest corner of the land of Moav. Thus, the land of Canaan across the Yardein to the west had its sourtheastern corner adjacent to Moav. 


Verse 4

<b>The border then turns south of Maaleh Akrabim.</b> Wherever it says “turns” or “extends,” it teaches that the border was not even, but swerved away. The border swerves, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>bending towards the north and angling west, so that the border passes south of Maaleh Akrabim — thus, Maaleh Akrabim was <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>within the border. 
<b>Passing toward Tzin.</b> צִנָה, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”to Tzin,” like מִצְרַיְמָה, “to Egypt.” 
<b>Its outskirts shall be.</b> Its ending, south of Kadeish Barne’a. 
<b>It shall extend to Chatzar Adar.</b> The border spreads, broadening towards the north and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>angling further west, until it reaches Chatzar Adar, from there to Atzmon, and from there to the Egyptian Estuary. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The term “turns” is used here, because it wrote “it shall extend to Chatzar Adar.” It began broadening after crossing Kadesh Barne’a, and the breadth of the strip which protruded northward reached from Kadesh Barne’a to Atzmon. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>From there and onward the border receded, turning toward the south until reaching the Egyptian Estuary, and from there west to the Mediterranean, which serves as the western border for all of Eretz Yisroel. Thus, the Egyptian Estuary is situated at the southwestern corner. 

Verse 5

<b>Its outskirts shall reach the sea.</b> Until the western border. The southern border no longer extends towards the west, past there. 

Verse 6

<b>As for the western border.</b> What is the western border?
<b>It shall be the Great (Mediterranean) Sea.</b> As a border.
<b>And its border.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The islands at sea are also part of the border. These islands are called “<i>isles</i>” in Old French.

Verse 7

<b>The northern border.</b> The northern border.
<b>From the Great (Mediterranean) Sea, turn yourselves to Hor Hahar.</b> Which is at the northwestern corner. Its peak slopes and enters the sea, with some of the expanse of the sea inward, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and some outward. 
<b>Turn.</b> Tilt yourselves to turn from west to north, to Mount Hor. 
<b>Turn.</b> The term denotes turning, as in “to the runners’ annex,” “the annexes of the gateway.” The annex, called “<i>apendiz</i>” in Old French, turns and slopes. 

Verse 8

<b>From Hor Hahar.</b> Turn and proceed along the northern border to the east, and you will encounter Levo Chamas — this is Antioch. 
<b>The outskirts of the border.</b> The end of the border. Wherever “the outskirts of the border” is said, either the border ends there completely without continuing further at all; or it digresses from there, broadens, and extends in another direction, proceeding further at an angle to the original expanse. It is in relation to the breadth of the original dimension that it is called “extremity,” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>for that dimension ends there. 

Verse 9

<b>Its outskirts shall be at Chatzar Einan.</b> This was the end of the northern border. Thus, Chatzar Einan was situated at the northeastern corner. From there, “turn yourselves to the eastern border.” 


Verse 10

<b>Turn.</b> The word [וְהִתְאַוִּיתֶם] denotes turning and tilting, like תְּתָאוּ . 
<b>To Shefam.</b> On the eastern border, and from there to Rivlah. 

Verse 11

<b>East of Ayin.</b> The name of a place. The border passes to its east, so that Ayin is situated within the border, and is part of Eretz Yisroel. 
<b>The border shall descend.</b> As the border proceeds from north to south, it continually descends. 
<b>And contact the bank of the eastern shore of the Kineres Sea.</b> So that Lake Kineres was within the border, to the west. The border is east of Lake Kineres, and descends from there to the Yardein. The Yardein flows diagonally, from north to south, angling towards the east, moves towards the land of Canaan at Lake Kineres and continues along the eastern side of Eretz Yisroel opposite Lake Kineres, until emptying into the Dead Sea. From there, the border closes with its extremity reaching the Dead Sea, from which the southeastern corner of the border began, thus surrounding it on all four sides. 


Verse 12



Verse 13



Verse 14



Verse 15

<b>To the east, toward the sunrise.</b> To the forefront of the world, which is east, as <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the eastern direction is called the forefront, and the western, the rear. Therefore, south is to the right, and north to the left. 


Verse 16



Verse 17

<b>Who shall inherit for you.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>For your sake. Each tribal leader was the guardian for his tribe, and <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>he apportioned the tribal inheritance to the families and individuals. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He chose a suitable portion for each individual, and their actions were binding, as if they had been designated as agents. But it would be improper to explain this לָכֶם [lit. “to you”] like every לָכֶם in Scripture, for, if so, it should have written יַנְחִילוּ לָכֶם, “they shall cause the inheritance to belong to you.” [לָכֶם] יִנְחֲלוּ means that they <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>shall inherit for you, for your sake, in your place, like ה' יִלָּחֵם לָכֶם, “God will wage war for your sake.” 


Verse 18

<b>To inherit the land.</b> He is to inherit, take the portion of the land as your surrogate. 

Verse 19



Verse 20



Verse 21



Verse 22



Verse 23



Verse 24



Verse 25



Verse 26



Verse 27



Verse 28



Verse 29

<b>To apportion the inheritance to Bnei Yisroel.</b> They are to give the inheritance to you according to its portions.

Chapter 35



Verse 1



Verse 2

<b>And open space.</b> Open space, an empty area surrounding the city, to beautify the city. One is not permitted to build a house there, or plant a vineyard, or sow seeds. 


Verse 3

<b>And all of their necessities to live.</b> For all their vital needs.

Verse 4

<b>A thousand <i>amos</i> all around.</b> But afterward it says, “two thousand <i>amos.</i>” How is this? He gave them two thousand (<i>amos</i>) all around the city. Of those, the inner thousand are for parkland, and the outer (thousand) are for fields and vineyards. 


Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8



Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11

<b>You shall provide.</b> הַקְרָיָיה means [nothing but] providing. Similarly, it says, “because the Adonoy your God provided for me.” 

Verse 12

<b>From the avenger.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Against the blood redeemer, who is the kinsman of the murder victim. 


Verse 13

<b>Six refuge cities.</b> This teaches that although Moshe designated three cities across the Yardein, during his lifetime, they did not absorb, until the selection of <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>the three that Yehoshua placed in the land of Canaan. 

Verse 14

<b>Three cities, etc.</b> Although there were, in the land of Canaan, nine tribes, and here only two and one half, the number of their cities of refuge was the same. Because Gil’ad was <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>rife 
with murderers, as it is written, “Gil’ad, city of evildoers, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>bloody ambush.” 

Verse 15



Verse 16

<b>But if he struck him with an iron instrument. </b> This does not refer to the inadvertent killing discussed in the preceding context, but, rather, to premeditated murder. It teaches that all implements of murder must be sizable enough to kill, for it is said, concerning all of them, “which can kill,” rendered by Targum [Onkelos], <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>”of a size capable of killing” — except for iron. For it is clearly evident to The Holy One, Blessed is He, that iron of any size can kill, even a needle. The Torah, therefore, did not specify a size by saying “which can kill.” Still, you may ask, “perhaps our passage refers to one who killed inadvertently?” <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>But it states, below, “or, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>with a stone which can kill, without seeing, etc.” This teaches that, in its statements above, Scripture refers to premeditated murder. 

Verse 17

<b>With a stone that can be held in the hand.</b> Large enough to fill the hand.
<b>Which can kill.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Large enough to kill, as rendered by Targum [Onkelos]. Since it is said, “if a man strikes his fellow with a stone” without specifying its size, perhaps any size? It is said, therefore, “which can kill.” 


Verse 18

<b>Or with a wooden implement [that can be held] in the hand.</b> Since it is said, “if a man strikes his slave or his maidservant with a rod,” perhaps any size? It is said, concerning wood, therefore, “which can cause death” — it must be sizable enough to kill. 

Verse 19

<b>Wherever he meets him.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Even inside the cities of refuge. 


Verse 20

<b>Deliberately.</b> As Targum [Onkelos] renders, בְּכַמְנָא, “from ambush.” 

Verse 21



Verse 22

<b>Suddenly.</b> Accidentally. Targum [Onkelos] renders בִּתְכֵיף, “suddenly.” He was nearby, and there was no time for him to take heed. 

Verse 23

<b>Or with a stone which can kill.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He struck him.
<b>Without seeing.</b> He did not see him. 

<b>He threw it down on him.</b> From here they (the Rabbis) said, “someone who kills <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>while descending, is exiled; [but if he kills] <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>while ascending, is not exiled.” 

Verse 24



Verse 25

<b>Until the death of the Kohein gadol.</b> As he causes the Divine Presence to reside in Israel, and lengthens their lives, while the murderer causes the Divine Presence to leave Israel, and shortens their lives, he (the murderer) is unworthy of being in the presence of the <i>Kohein Gadol</i>. Another interpretation: Because the <i>Kohein Gadol</i> should have prayed <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>that this pitfall not occur in Israel during his lifetime. 
<b>Who was anointed with the sacred oil.</b> According to its plain meaning, this is one of the shortened passages, as it does not explain <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>who anointed him, but, rather, as if to say, “whom, whoever anointed him with the sacred oil.” Our sages expound this, in <i>Maseches</i> Makos, as verification of a teaching, to teach that, if before his case was decided, the <i>Kohein Gadol</i> died and another was appointed in his place, and his case was then decided, he is released from exile at the death of the second, as it is said, “whom he anointed.” Was it he who anointed him as a <i>kohein,</i> or a <i>kohein</i> who anointed him? Therefore, this is meant to include one who was anointed in his days — that he is released from exile at his death. 

Verse 26



Verse 27

<b>lit. He has no blood.</b> It is as if he had murdered a lifeless man, as his blood is forfeit. 


Verse 28



Verse 29

<b>In all your dwelling places.</b> This teaches that the lower Sanhedrin court functions outside the land <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>so long as it functions in Eretz Yisroel.

Verse 30

<b>If anyone lls a person, etc.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>The one who endeavors to kill him because he had killed a person. . . 
<b>Upon the testimony of witnesses shall [the murderer] be killed.</b> Who testify that the murderer acted intentionally, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and was forwarned. 

Verse 31

<b>And do not accept atonement compensation.</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>He cannot absolve himself with money

Verse 32

<b>And, do not accept atonement compensation for one who has fled to his refuge city.</b> For, someone who fled to a refuge city because he killed inadvertently, is not absolved from exile with money, by paying atonement compensation so that he may return and dwell in the land before the <i>kohein</i> dies. 
<b> לָנוּס .</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Like לְנָס, as in שׁוּבֵי מִלְחָמָה, “who returned from battle.” Similarly, נוּגֵי מִמּוֹעֵד, “who were excluded from the festivals.” Similarly, כִּי מֻלִים הָיוּ, “for they were circumcised.” Just as one says שׁוּב concerning someone who has already returned, and מוּל concerning someone who was already circumcised, so does one say לָנוּס concerning someone who has already fled. He is called נוּס as if to say מֻבְרָח, “has fled.” But perhaps you might interpret לָנוּס as לִבְרוֹחַ,”to flee,” and explain “do not accept atonement compensation” “for someone who must flee,” and absolve him from exile? Then I do not know how it could say “so that he may return and dwell in the land,” when he did not yet flee — from where shall he return? 

Verse 33

<b>Do not pollute (lit. falsely flatter).</b> <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Do not bring evil, as Targum [Onkelos] renders, וְלָא תְחַיְּבוּן, “do not bring guilt.” 


Verse 34

<b>Wherein I reside.</b> Do not cause Me to reside in its defilement.
<b>For I, Adonoy, dwell among Bnei Yisroel.</b> Even when they are defiled, the Divine Presence rests among them. 

Chapter 36



Verse 1



Verse 2



Verse 3

<b>And it will be added to the inheritance of the tribe.</b> Since her son is her heir, and the son’s tribal kinship follows his father’s. 


Verse 4

<b>And if the yoveil occurs.</b> From here <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>R’ Yehudah said that <i>yoveil</i> is destined <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>to discontinue.
<b>And if the <i>yoveil</i> occurs.</b> As if to say, this is not a sale, which reverts on <i>yoveil</i>, for an inheritance does not revert on <i>yoveil.</i> So even if <i>yoveil</i> occurs, the inheritance will not revert to its tribe, and will thus be added to the inheritance of the tribe into which they marry. 


Verse 5



Verse 6



Verse 7



Verse 8

<b>Every daughter who inherits property.</b> When her father had no son. 


Verse 9



Verse 10



Verse 11

<b>Machlah, Sirtzah, etc.</b> Here they are counted by seniority, <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>and they were married in order of their birth. <i data-commentator="Siftei Chakhamim" data-label="⚬"></i>Throughout Scripture, they are counted according to their wisdom. This teaches that they were all equal[ly esteemed.]
